<p><b>Franconia</b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Franken</i></span>, also called <i>Frankenland</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Region" title="Region">region</a> in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, characterised by its culture and language, and may be roughly associated with the areas in which the <a href="/wiki/East_Franconian_German" title="East Franconian German">East Franconian dialect group</a>, locally referred to as <i>fränkisch</i>, is spoken.<sup id="cite_ref-fr.C3.A4nkisches_dialekt_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fr.C3.A4nkisches_dialekt-1">[1]</a></sup> It commonly refers to the eastern part of the historical <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Franconia" title="Duchy of Franconia">Franconian stem duchy</a>, mainly represented by the modern <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavarian</a> administrative districts of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Franconia" title="Lower Franconia">Lower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_Franconia" title="Middle Franconia">Middle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Upper_Franconia" title="Upper Franconia">Upper Franconia</a>, the adjacent northeastern parts of <a href="/wiki/Heilbronn-Franken" title="Heilbronn-Franken">Heilbronn-Franken</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, parts of <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a> south of the <a href="/wiki/Rennsteig" title="Rennsteig">Rennsteig</a> ridge, and small parts of <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>. However, there is no fixed area that is officially defined as Franconia.</p>
<p>The German word <i>Franken</i> - Franconians - also refers to the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a>, which is mainly to be found in this region. They are to be distinguished from the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> tribe of the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>, and historically formed their easternmost settlement area. The origins of Franconia lie in the settlement of the Franks from the 6th&#160;century in the area probably populated until then mainly by the <a href="/wiki/Elbe_Germanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Elbe Germanic">Elbe Germanic</a> people in the <a href="/wiki/River_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="River Main">Main</a> river area. Known from the 9th&#160;century as <i>Francia Orientalis</i> (East Francia).<sup id="cite_ref-francia_orientalis_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-francia_orientalis-2">[2]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> the region formed much of the eastern part of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Franconia" title="Duchy of Franconia">Duchy of Franconia</a> and, from 1500, the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Circle" title="Franconian Circle">Franconian Circle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-reichskreis2_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reichskreis2-3">[3]</a></sup> In the course of the restructuring of the south German states by <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> after the demise of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, most of Franconia was awarded to Bavaria.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The German name for Franconia, <i>Franken</i>, comes from the <a href="/wiki/Dative" class="mw-redirect" title="Dative">dative</a> plural form of <i>Franke,</i> a member of the Germanic tribe known as the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Onomatology" class="mw-redirect" title="Onomatology">onomatologists</a> largely follow the reference book compiled by <a href="/wiki/Early_medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Early medieval">early medieval</a> scholar, Saint <a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a>, (c. 560–636) and state that the name derives from an <a href="/wiki/Indo-Germanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Germanic">Indo-Germanic</a> root, <i>*(s)p(h)ereg-</i> ("avaricious" or "ferocious"). This syllable occurs in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Dutch" title="Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a> <i>vrac</i>, "avaricious", and old <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a> <i>frakkr</i>, "quick, bold", and means something like "brave, daring, courageous". According to this the Franks were thus the "brave ones", "courageous ones" or "audacious ones".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> From the 9th century the geographical name no longer referred to the whole of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, but increasingly to the region along the River Main, where the name finally stuck.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The German word <i>frank</i> in the sense of "free" is, by contrast, not an original description of the Franks, but emerged at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Merovingians" class="mw-redirect" title="Merovingians">Merovingians</a> in the Romanised principality of the Franks. Not until the 15th century was the German word <i>frei</i> ("free") borrowed from the French.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franconia_details.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Franconia_details.png/320px-Franconia_details.png" width="320" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Franconia_details.png/480px-Franconia_details.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Franconia_details.png/640px-Franconia_details.png 2x" data-file-width="1180" data-file-height="825" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franconia_details.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The present-day Upper, Lower, and Middle Franconian administrative districts (in blue), with adjacent East Franconian language areas in Thuringia (red) and in Baden-Württemberg (yellow)</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Franconian lands lie principally in Bavaria, north and south of the sinuous <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">River Main</a> which, together with the left (southern) <a href="/wiki/Regnitz" title="Regnitz">Regnitz</a> tributary, including its <a href="/wiki/Rednitz" title="Rednitz">Rednitz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pegnitz_(river)" title="Pegnitz (river)">Pegnitz</a> headstreams, drains most of Franconia. Other large rivers include the upper <a href="/wiki/Werra" title="Werra">Werra</a> in Thuringia and the <a href="/wiki/Tauber" title="Tauber">Tauber</a>, as well as the upper <a href="/wiki/Jagst" title="Jagst">Jagst</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kocher" title="Kocher">Kocher</a> streams in the west, both right tributaries of the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a>. In southern Middle Franconia, the <a href="/wiki/Altm%C3%BChl" title="Altmühl">Altmühl</a> flows towards the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Rhine%E2%80%93Main%E2%80%93Danube_Canal" title="Rhine–Main–Danube Canal">Rhine–Main–Danube Canal</a> crosses the <a href="/wiki/European_Watershed" class="mw-redirect" title="European Watershed">European Watershed</a>. The man-made <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Lake_District" title="Franconian Lake District">Franconian Lake District</a> has become a popular destination for day-trippers and tourists.</p>
<p>The landscape is characterized by numerous <i><a href="/wiki/Mittelgebirge" title="Mittelgebirge">Mittelgebirge</a></i> ranges of the German <a href="/wiki/Central_Uplands" title="Central Uplands">Central Uplands</a>. The Western natural border of Franconia is formed by the <a href="/wiki/Spessart" title="Spessart">Spessart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B6n_Mountains" title="Rhön Mountains">Rhön Mountains</a>, separating it from the former <a href="/wiki/Rhenish_Franconia" title="Rhenish Franconia">Rhenish Franconian</a> lands around <a href="/wiki/Aschaffenburg" title="Aschaffenburg">Aschaffenburg</a> (officially part of Lower Franconia), whose inhabitants speak <a href="/wiki/Hessian_dialects" title="Hessian dialects">Hessian dialects</a>. To the north rise the <a href="/wiki/Rennsteig" title="Rennsteig">Rennsteig</a> ridge of the <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_Forest" title="Thuringian Forest">Thuringian Forest</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_Highland" title="Thuringian Highland">Thuringian Highland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Forest" title="Franconian Forest">Franconian Forest</a>, the border with the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Saxony" title="Upper Saxony">Upper Saxon</a> lands of <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a>. The Franconian lands include the present-day South Thuringian districts of <a href="/wiki/Schmalkalden-Meiningen" title="Schmalkalden-Meiningen">Schmalkalden-Meiningen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hildburghausen_(district)" title="Hildburghausen (district)">Hildburghausen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sonneberg_(district)" title="Sonneberg (district)">Sonneberg</a>, the historical <i><a href="/wiki/Gau_(country_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gau (country subdivision)">Gau</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Grabfeld" title="Grabfeld">Grabfeld</a>, held by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Henneberg" title="House of Henneberg">House of Henneberg</a> from the 11th century and later part of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wettin" title="House of Wettin">Wettin</a> duchy of <a href="/wiki/Saxe-Meiningen" title="Saxe-Meiningen">Saxe-Meiningen</a>.</p>
<p>In the east, the <a href="/wiki/Fichtel_Mountains" title="Fichtel Mountains">Fichtel Mountains</a> lead to <a href="/wiki/Vogtland" title="Vogtland">Vogtland</a>, Bohemian <a href="/wiki/Egerland" title="Egerland">Egerland</a> (<i>Chebsko</i>) in the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, and the Bavarian <a href="/wiki/Upper_Palatinate" title="Upper Palatinate">Upper Palatinate</a>. The hills of the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Jura" title="Franconian Jura">Franconian Jura</a> in the south mark the border with the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">Upper Bavarian</a> region (<i><a href="/wiki/Altbayern" title="Altbayern">Altbayern</a></i>), historical <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabia</a>, and the Danube basin. The northern parts of the Upper Bavarian <a href="/wiki/Eichst%C3%A4tt_(district)" title="Eichstätt (district)">Eichstätt District</a>, territory of the historical <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Eichst%C3%A4tt" title="Bishopric of Eichstätt">Bishopric of Eichstätt</a>, are also counted as part of Franconia.</p>
<p>In the west, Franconia proper comprises the <a href="/wiki/Tauber_Franconia" title="Tauber Franconia">Tauber Franconia</a> region along the Tauber river, which As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is largely part of the <a href="/wiki/Main-Tauber-Kreis" title="Main-Tauber-Kreis">Main-Tauber-Kreis</a> in Baden-Württemberg. The state's larger <a href="/wiki/Heilbronn-Franken" title="Heilbronn-Franken">Heilbronn-Franken</a> region also includes the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Hohenlohe_(district)" title="Hohenlohe (district)">Hohenlohe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Schw%C3%A4bisch_Hall_(district)" title="Schwäbisch Hall (district)">Schwäbisch Hall districts</a>. In the city of <a href="/wiki/Heilbronn" title="Heilbronn">Heilbronn</a>, beyond the <a href="/wiki/Haller_Ebene" class="mw-redirect" title="Haller Ebene">Haller Ebene</a> plateau, <a href="/wiki/South_Franconian_German" title="South Franconian German">South Franconian</a> dialects are spoken. Furthermore, in those easternmost parts of the <a href="/wiki/Neckar-Odenwald-Kreis" title="Neckar-Odenwald-Kreis">Neckar-Odenwald-Kreis</a> which had formerly belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Bishopric of Würzburg">Bishopric of Würzburg</a>, the inhabitants have preserved their Franconian identity. Franconian areas in <a href="/wiki/East_Hesse" title="East Hesse">East Hesse</a> along Spessart and Rhön comprise <a href="/wiki/Gersfeld" title="Gersfeld">Gersfeld</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ehrenberg,_Hesse" title="Ehrenberg, Hesse">Ehrenberg</a>.</p>
<p>The two largest cities of Franconia are <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>. Though located on the southeastern periphery of the area, the Nuremberg metropolitan area is often identified as the economic and cultural centre of Franconia. Further cities in Bavarian Franconia include <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrth" title="Fürth">Fürth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erlangen" title="Erlangen">Erlangen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bayreuth" title="Bayreuth">Bayreuth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bamberg" title="Bamberg">Bamberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aschaffenburg" title="Aschaffenburg">Aschaffenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schweinfurt" title="Schweinfurt">Schweinfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hof,_Bavaria" title="Hof, Bavaria">Hof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coburg" title="Coburg">Coburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ansbach" title="Ansbach">Ansbach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Schwabach" title="Schwabach">Schwabach</a>. The major (East) Franconian towns in Baden-Württemberg are <a href="/wiki/Schw%C3%A4bisch_Hall" title="Schwäbisch Hall">Schwäbisch Hall</a> on the Kocher — the <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">imperial city</a> declared itself "Swabian" in 1442 — and <a href="/wiki/Crailsheim" title="Crailsheim">Crailsheim</a> on the Jagst river. The main towns in Thuringia are <a href="/wiki/Suhl" title="Suhl">Suhl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meiningen" title="Meiningen">Meiningen</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent">Extent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Extent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sakristei-Mgn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Sakristei-Mgn.jpg/220px-Sakristei-Mgn.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Sakristei-Mgn.jpg/330px-Sakristei-Mgn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Sakristei-Mgn.jpg/440px-Sakristei-Mgn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1168" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sakristei-Mgn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i><a href="/wiki/Franconian_Rake" title="Franconian Rake">Franconian Rake</a></i> may be used as an indicator of whether a place is part of Franconia.<br />
Here: the vestry of Meiningen's municipal church in South Thuringia. The Franconian Rake may be seen on the left</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Franconia may be distinguished from the regions that surround it by its peculiar historical factors and its cultural and especially linguistic characteristics, but it is not a political entity with a fixed or tightly defined area. As a result, it is debated whether some areas belong to Franconia or not. Pointers to a more precise definition of Franconia's boundaries include: the territories covered by the former <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Franconia" title="Duchy of Franconia">Duchy of Franconia</a> and former <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Circle" title="Franconian Circle">Franconian Circle</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-reichskreis3_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reichskreis3-11">[11]</a></sup> the range of the <a href="/wiki/East_Franconian_dialect_group" class="mw-redirect" title="East Franconian dialect group">East Franconian dialect group</a>, the common culture and history of the region and the use of the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Rake" title="Franconian Rake">Franconian Rake</a> on coats of arms, flags and seals. However, a sense of popular consciousness of being Franconian is only detectable from the 19th century onwards, which is why the circumstances of the emergence of a Frankish identity are disputed.<sup id="cite_ref-bayernradio_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bayernradio-12">[12]</a></sup> Franconia has many cultural peculiarities which have been adopted from other regions and further developed.<sup id="cite_ref-bayernradio_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bayernradio-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following regions are counted as part of Franconia today: the Bavarian <a href="/wiki/Regierungsbezirk" title="Regierungsbezirk">provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Franconia" title="Lower Franconia">Lower Franconia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upper_Franconia" title="Upper Franconia">Upper Franconia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Franconia" title="Middle Franconia">Middle Franconia</a>, the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Pyrbaum" title="Pyrbaum">Pyrbaum</a> in the county of <a href="/wiki/Neumarkt_in_der_Oberpfalz_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neumarkt in der Oberpfalz (district)">Neumarkt in der Oberpfalz</a>, the northwestern part of the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">Upper Bavarian</a> county of <a href="/wiki/Eichst%C3%A4tt_(district)" title="Eichstätt (district)">Eichstätt</a> (covering the same area as the old county of Alt-Eichstätt), the East Franconian counties of <a href="/wiki/South_Thuringia" title="South Thuringia">South Thuringia</a>, parts of <a href="/wiki/Fulda_(district)" title="Fulda (district)">Fulda</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Odenwaldkreis" title="Odenwaldkreis">Odenwaldkreis</a> in Hesse, the Baden-Württemberg regions of <a href="/wiki/Tauber_Franconia" title="Tauber Franconia">Tauber Franconia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hohenlohe" title="Hohenlohe">Hohenlohe</a> as well as the region around the Badenian <a href="/wiki/Buchen_(Odenwald)" class="mw-redirect" title="Buchen (Odenwald)">Buchen</a>.</p>
<p>In individual cases the membership of some areas is disputed. These include the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">Bavarian language</a> area of Alt-<a href="/wiki/Eichst%C3%A4tt" title="Eichstätt">Eichstätt</a><sup id="cite_ref-bayernradio_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bayernradio-12">[12]</a></sup> and the Hessian-speaking<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> region around <a href="/wiki/Aschaffenburg" title="Aschaffenburg">Aschaffenburg</a>, which was never part of the Franconian Imperial Circle. The affiliation of the city of <a href="/wiki/Heilbronn" title="Heilbronn">Heilbronn</a>, whose inhabitants do not call themselves Franks,<sup id="cite_ref-heilbronn_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heilbronn-14">[14]</a></sup> is also controversial. Moreover, the sense of belonging to Franconia in the Frankish-speaking areas of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Palatinate" title="Upper Palatinate">Upper Palatinate</a>, South Thuringia<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and Hesse is sometimes less marked.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franken_2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Franken_2.svg/170px-Franken_2.svg.png" width="170" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Franken_2.svg/255px-Franken_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Franken_2.svg/340px-Franken_2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1227" data-file-height="1236" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franken_2.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bavarian provinces of Upper, Middle and Lower Franconia</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baden_Wuerttemberg_Region_Heilbronn-Franken.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Baden_Wuerttemberg_Region_Heilbronn-Franken.svg/220px-Baden_Wuerttemberg_Region_Heilbronn-Franken.svg.png" width="220" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Baden_Wuerttemberg_Region_Heilbronn-Franken.svg/330px-Baden_Wuerttemberg_Region_Heilbronn-Franken.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Baden_Wuerttemberg_Region_Heilbronn-Franken.svg/440px-Baden_Wuerttemberg_Region_Heilbronn-Franken.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1179" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baden_Wuerttemberg_Region_Heilbronn-Franken.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The region of Heilbronn-Franconia in Baden-Württemberg</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The region of Franconia is divided among the states of Hesse, Thuringia, Bavaria and Baden-Württemberg. The largest part of Franconia, both by population and area, belongs to the Free State of Bavaria and is divided into the three provinces (<i>Regierungsbezirke</i>) of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Franconia" title="Middle Franconia">Middle Franconia</a> (capital: <a href="/wiki/Ansbach" title="Ansbach">Ansbach</a>), <a href="/wiki/Upper_Franconia" title="Upper Franconia">Upper Franconia</a> (capital: <a href="/wiki/Bayreuth" title="Bayreuth">Bayreuth</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Franconia" title="Lower Franconia">Lower Franconia</a> (capital: <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>). The name of these provinces, as in the case of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">Upper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Bavaria" title="Lower Bavaria">Lower Bavaria</a>, refers to their situation with respect to the <a href="/wiki/River_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="River Main">River Main</a>. Thuse Upper Franconia lies on the upper reaches of the river, Lower Franconia on its lower reaches and Middle Franconia lies in between, although the Main does not flow through Middle Franconia itself. Where the boundaries of these three provinces meet (the '<a href="/wiki/Tripoint" title="Tripoint">tripoint</a>') is the <i><a href="/wiki/Dreifrankenstein" title="Dreifrankenstein">Dreifrankenstein</a></i> ("Three Franconias Rock").<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Small parts of Franconia also belong to the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Palatinate" title="Upper Palatinate">Upper Palatinate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">Upper Bavaria</a>.</p>
<p>The Franconian territories of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a> are the regions of <a href="/wiki/Tauber_Franconia" title="Tauber Franconia">Tauber Franconia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hohenlohe" title="Hohenlohe">Hohenlohe</a>, which belong to the <a href="/wiki/Heilbronn-Franconia_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Heilbronn-Franconia Region">Heilbronn-Franconia Region</a> with its office in Heilbronn and are part of the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Region" title="Stuttgart Region">Stuttgart Region</a>, and the area around the Badenian <a href="/wiki/Buchen_(Odenwald)" class="mw-redirect" title="Buchen (Odenwald)">Buchen</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Neckar" title="Rhine-Neckar">Rhein-Neckar Region</a>. The Franconian parts of Thuringia (<a href="/wiki/Henneberg_Franconia" title="Henneberg Franconia">Henneberg Franconia</a>) lie within the Southwest Thuringia Planning Region. The Franconian regions in Hesse form the smaller parts of the counties of <a href="/wiki/Fulda_(district)" title="Fulda (district)">Fulda</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kassel_province" class="mw-redirect" title="Kassel province">Kassel province</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Odenwaldkreis" title="Odenwaldkreis">Odenwaldkreis</a> (<a href="/wiki/Darmstadt_province" class="mw-redirect" title="Darmstadt province">Darmstadt province</a>), or lie on the border with Bavaria or Thuringia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivers_and_lakes">Rivers and lakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rivers and lakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brombach_luft.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Brombach_luft.jpg/220px-Brombach_luft.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Brombach_luft.jpg/330px-Brombach_luft.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Brombach_luft.jpg/440px-Brombach_luft.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brombach_luft.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The lake of <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fer_Brombachsee" title="Großer Brombachsee">Großer Brombachsee</a>. View over <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ramsberg_am_Brombachsee&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ramsberg am Brombachsee (page does not exist)">Ramsberg</a> looking east towards the dam</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The two most important rivers of the region are the <a href="/wiki/River_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="River Main">Main</a> and its primary tributary, the <a href="/wiki/Regnitz" title="Regnitz">Regnitz</a>. The tributaries of these two rivers in Franconia are the <a href="/wiki/Tauber" title="Tauber">Tauber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pegnitz_(river)" title="Pegnitz (river)">Pegnitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rednitz" title="Rednitz">Rednitz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Saale" title="Franconian Saale">Franconian Saale</a>. Other major rivers in the region are the <a href="/wiki/Jagst" title="Jagst">Jagst</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kocher_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kocher (river)">Kocher</a> in Hohenlohe-Franconia, which empty into the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> north of Heilbronn in Baden-Württemberg, the <a href="/wiki/Altm%C3%BChl" title="Altmühl">Altmühl</a> and the <a href="/wiki/W%C3%B6rnitz" title="Wörnitz">Wörnitz</a> in Middle Franconia, both tributaries of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, and the upper and middle reaches of the <a href="/wiki/Werra" title="Werra">Werra</a>, the right-hand headstream of the <a href="/wiki/Weser" title="Weser">Weser</a>. In the northeast of Upper Franconia rise two left-hand tributaries of the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Saxon_Saale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saxon Saale">Saxon Saale</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eger_(Elbe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eger (Elbe)">Eger</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Main-Danube_Canal" class="mw-redirect" title="Main-Danube Canal">Main-Danube Canal</a> connects the Main and Danube across Franconia, running from Bamberg via Nuremberg to <a href="/wiki/Kelheim" title="Kelheim">Kelheim</a>. It thus complements the Rhine, Main and Danube, helping to ensure a continuous navigable waterway between the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. In Franconia, there are only a few, often very small, natural <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">lakes</a>. This is due to fact that most natural lakes in Germany are <a href="/wiki/Glacial_lake" title="Glacial lake">glacial</a> or <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">volcanic</a> in origin, and Franconia escaped both influences in recent earth history. Among the largest waterbodies are <a href="/wiki/Reservoir" title="Reservoir">reservoirs</a>, which are mostly used as water reserves for the relatively dry landscapes of Franconia. These includes the waters of the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Lake_District" title="Franconian Lake District">Franconian Lake District</a>, which was established in the 1970s and is also a tourist attraction. The heart of these lakes is the <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fer_Brombachsee" title="Großer Brombachsee">Großer Brombachsee</a>, which has an area of 8.7&#160;km² and is thus the largest waterbody in Franconia by surface area.</p>
<h3><span id="Hills,_mountains_and_plains"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hills.2C_mountains_and_plains">Hills, mountains and plains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hills, mountains and plains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several <a href="/wiki/Central_Upland" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Upland">Central Upland</a> ranges dominate the Franconian countryside. In the southeast,Franconia is shielded from the rest of Bavaria by the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Jura" title="Franconian Jura">Franconian Jura</a>. In the east, the <a href="/wiki/Fichtel_Mountains" title="Fichtel Mountains">Fichtel Mountains</a> form the border; in the north are <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Forest" title="Franconian Forest">Franconian Forest</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_Forest" title="Thuringian Forest">Thuringian Forest</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B6n_Mountains" title="Rhön Mountains">Rhön Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spessart" title="Spessart">Spessart</a> form a kind of natural barrier. To the west are the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Heights" title="Franconian Heights">Franconian Heights</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Swabian-Franconian_Forest" title="Swabian-Franconian Forest">Swabian-Franconian Forest</a>. In the Franconian part of South Hesse is the <a href="/wiki/Odenwald" title="Odenwald">Odenwald</a>. Parts of the southern <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_Forest" title="Thuringian Forest">Thuringian Forest</a> border on Franconia. The most important hill ranges in the interior of the region are the <a href="/wiki/Steigerwald" title="Steigerwald">Steigerwald</a> and the Franconian Jura with their sub-ranges of <a href="/wiki/Hahnenkamm_(Altm%C3%BChltal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hahnenkamm (Altmühltal)">Hahnenkamm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Switzerland" title="Franconian Switzerland">Franconian Switzerland</a>. The highest mountain in Franconia is the <a href="/wiki/Schneeberg_(Fichtel_Mountains)" title="Schneeberg (Fichtel Mountains)">Schneeberg</a> in the Fichtel Mountains which is <span style="border-width:0px; padding:0px; margin:0px;">1,051&#160;m&#160;above&#160;<a href="/wiki/Normalh%C3%B6hennull" title="Normalhöhennull">sea level (NHN)</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-geoquelle_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geoquelle-17">[17]</a></sup> Other well-known mountains include the <a href="/wiki/Ochsenkopf_(Fichtel_Mountains)" title="Ochsenkopf (Fichtel Mountains)">Ochsenkopf</a> (1,024m<sup id="cite_ref-geoquelle_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geoquelle-17">[17]</a></sup>), the <a href="/wiki/Kreuzberg_(Rh%C3%B6n)" title="Kreuzberg (Rhön)">Kreuzberg</a> (927.8m<sup id="cite_ref-geoquelle_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geoquelle-17">[17]</a></sup>) and the <a href="/wiki/Hesselberg" title="Hesselberg">Hesselberg</a> (689.4m<sup id="cite_ref-geoquelle_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geoquelle-17">[17]</a></sup>). The <a href="/wiki/Inliers_and_outliers_(geology)" title="Inliers and outliers (geology)">outliers</a> of the region include the Hesselberg and the <a href="/wiki/Gleichberge" title="Gleichberge">Gleichberge</a>. The lowest point in Franconia is the water level of the River Main in <a href="/wiki/Kahl_am_Main" title="Kahl am Main">Kahl</a> which lies at a height of 100 metres above sea level.</p>
<p>In addition to the hill and mountain ranges, there are also several very level areas, including the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Middle_Franconian_Basin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Middle Franconian Basin (page does not exist)">Middle Franconian Basin</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hohenlohe_Plain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hohenlohe Plain (page does not exist)">Hohenlohe Plain</a>. In the south of Franconia are smaller parts of the flat <a href="/wiki/N%C3%B6rdlinger_Ries" title="Nördlinger Ries">Nördlinger Ries</a>, one of the best preserved impact craters on earth.</p>
<h3><span id="Forests,_reserves,_flora_and_fauna"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Forests.2C_reserves.2C_flora_and_fauna">Forests, reserves, flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Forests, reserves, flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steinerne_Rinne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Steinerne_Rinne.jpg/170px-Steinerne_Rinne.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Steinerne_Rinne.jpg/255px-Steinerne_Rinne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Steinerne_Rinne.jpg/340px-Steinerne_Rinne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steinerne_Rinne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Steinerne_Rinne&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Steinerne Rinne (page does not exist)">Steinerne Rinne</a> near Rohrbach, <a href="/wiki/Ettenstatt" title="Ettenstatt">Ettenstatt</a>, county of <a href="/wiki/Wei%C3%9Fenburg-Gunzenhausen" title="Weißenburg-Gunzenhausen">Weißenburg-Gunzenhausen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Franconia's flora is dominated by deciduous and coniferous forests. Natural forests in Franconia occur mainly in the ranges of the Spessart, Franconian Forest, Odenwald and Steigerwald. The Nuremberg <i>Reichswald</i> is another great <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forest</a>, located within the metropolitan region of Nuremberg. Other large areas of forest in the region are the <a href="/w/index.php?title=M%C3%B6nchswald&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mönchswald (page does not exist)">Mönchswald</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Reichsforst_(Fichtel)" title="Reichsforst (Fichtel)">Reichsforst</a> in the Fichtel Mountains and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Selb_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Selb Forest (page does not exist)">Selb Forest</a>. In the river valleys along the Main and Tauber, the countryside was developed for viticulture. In Spessart there are great oak forests. Also widespread are <a href="/wiki/Calcareous_grassland" title="Calcareous grassland">calcareous grasslands</a>, extensively used <a href="/wiki/Pasture" title="Pasture">pastures</a> on very <a href="/wiki/Nutrient_(plant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nutrient (plant)">oligotrophic</a>, poor sites. In particular, the southern <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Jura" title="Franconian Jura">Franconian Jura</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Altm%C3%BChl_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Altmühl Valley">Altmühl Valley</a>, is characterized by poor grassland of this type. Many of these places have been designated as a <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected areas</a>.</p>
<p>Franconia has several regions with sandy habitats that are unique for south Germany and are protected as the so-called Sand Belt of Franconia or <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandachse_Franken&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sandachse Franken (page does not exist)">Sandachse Franken</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> When the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Altm%C3%BChlsee&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Altmühlsee (page does not exist)">Altmühlsee</a> reservoir was built, a bird island was created and designated as a nature reserve where a variety of birds nest. Another important reserve is the <a href="/wiki/Black_Moor_(Rh%C3%B6n)" title="Black Moor (Rhön)">Black Moor</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B6n" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhön">Rhön</a>, which is one of the most important bog areas in Central Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> A well known reserve is the <a href="/wiki/Luisenburg_Rock_Labyrinth" title="Luisenburg Rock Labyrinth">Luisenburg Rock Labyrinth</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wunsiedel" title="Wunsiedel">Wunsiedel</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Felsenmeer" class="mw-redirect" title="Felsenmeer">felsenmeer</a> of <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> blocks up to several metres across. The establishment of the first Franconian <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national park</a> in the Steigerwald caused controversy and its designation was rejected in July 2011 by the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Bavarian government">Bavarian government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-natur_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natur-20">[20]</a></sup> The reason was the negative attitude of local population. Conservationists are now demanding protection for parts of the Steigerwald by nominating it for a World Heritage Site.<sup id="cite_ref-natur_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natur-20">[20]</a></sup> There are several <a href="/wiki/Nature_park" title="Nature park">nature parks</a> in Franconia, including the <a href="/wiki/Altm%C3%BChl_Valley_Nature_Park" title="Altmühl Valley Nature Park">Altmühl Valley Nature Park</a>, which, since 1969, has been one of the largest in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other <a href="/wiki/Nature_park" title="Nature park">nature parks</a> are the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Swabian-Franconian_Forest_Nature_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Swabian-Franconian Forest Nature Park (page does not exist)">Swabian-Franconian Forest Nature Park</a> in Baden-Württemberg, and the nature parks of <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Rh%C3%B6n_Nature_Park" title="Bavarian Rhön Nature Park">Bavarian Rhön</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fichtel_Mountain_Nature_Park" title="Fichtel Mountain Nature Park">Fichtel Mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Heights_Nature_Park" title="Franconian Heights Nature Park">Franconian Heights</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconian_Forest_Nature_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Franconian Forest Nature Park (page does not exist)">Franconian Forest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Switzerland-Veldenstein_Forest_Nature_Park" title="Franconian Switzerland-Veldenstein Forest Nature Park">Franconian Switzerland-Veldenstein Forest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ha%C3%9Fberge_Nature_Park" title="Haßberge Nature Park">Haßberge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spessart_Nature_Park" title="Spessart Nature Park">Spessart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steigerwald_Nature_Park" title="Steigerwald Nature Park">Steigerwald</a> in Bavaria, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Bergstra%C3%9Fe-Odenwald_Nature_Park" title="Bergstraße-Odenwald Nature Park">Bergstraße-Odenwald Nature Park</a> which straddles Bavaria, Baden-Württemberg and Hesse. Nature parks cover almost half the area of Franconia.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1991 <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> recognised the Rhön as a <a href="/wiki/Biosph%C3%A4renreservat_Rh%C3%B6n" class="mw-redirect" title="Biosphärenreservat Rhön">biosphere reserve</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Among the most picturesque geotopes in Bavaria, are the Franconian sites of <i><a href="/wiki/Fossa_Carolina" title="Fossa Carolina">Fossa Carolina</a></i>, the Twelve Apostle Rocks (<i>Zwölf-Apostel-Felsen</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Ehrenb%C3%BCrg" title="Ehrenbürg">Ehrenbürg</a>, the cave ruins of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Riesenburg_(cave)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Riesenburg (cave) (page does not exist)">Riesenburg</a> and the lake of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Frickenh%C3%A4user_See&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Frickenhäuser See (page does not exist)">Frickenhäuser See</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Bird_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="European Bird Reserve">European Bird Reserves</a> in Franconia are found mainly in uplands like the Steigerwald, in large forests like Nuremberg's Imperial Forest or along rivers like the Altmühl.<sup id="cite_ref-abc_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc-25">[25]</a></sup> There are also numerous <a href="/wiki/Special_Areas_of_Conservation" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Areas of Conservation">Special Areas of Conservation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protected_landscape" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected landscape">protected landscapes</a>. In Franconia there are very many <a href="/wiki/Tufa" title="Tufa">tufas</a>, raised stream beds near river sources within the <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> landscape that are known as 'stone runnels' (<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steinerne_Rinne&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Steinerne Rinne (page does not exist)">Steinerne Rinnen</a></i>). There are protected examples at <a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%A4srinne&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Käsrinne (page does not exist)">Heidenheim</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Steinerne_Rinne_(Wolfsbronn)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Steinerne Rinne (Wolfsbronn) (page does not exist)">Wolfsbronn</a>.</p>
<p>Like large parts of Germany, Franconia only has a few large species of wild animal. Forest dwellers include various species of <a href="/wiki/Marten" title="Marten">marten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fallow_deer" title="Fallow deer">fallow deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_deer" title="Red deer">red deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">roe deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">fox</a>. In natural areas such as the Fichtel mountains there are populations of <a href="/wiki/European_lynx" class="mw-redirect" title="European lynx">lynx</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capercaillie" class="mw-redirect" title="Capercaillie">capercaillie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Fichtel_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fichtel-26">[26]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/European_beaver" class="mw-redirect" title="European beaver">beaver</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_otter" class="mw-redirect" title="European otter">otter</a> have grown in numbers. There are occasional sightings of animals that had long been extinct in Central Europe, for example, the <a href="/wiki/European_wolf" class="mw-redirect" title="European wolf">wolf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
