<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Only in the extreme northeast of Franconia and in the Spessart are there <a href="/wiki/Variscan" class="mw-redirect" title="Variscan">Variscan</a> <a href="/wiki/Outcrop" title="Outcrop">outcrops</a> of the crystalline <a href="/wiki/Basement_(geology)" title="Basement (geology)">basement</a>, which were uplifted from below the surface when the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> exerted a northwards-oriented pressure. These are rocks of pre-<a href="/wiki/Permian" title="Permian">Permian</a> vintage, which were folded during various stages of <a href="/wiki/Variscan_orogeny" title="Variscan orogeny">Variscan orogeny</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Late_Palaeozoic" class="mw-redirect" title="Late Palaeozoic">Late Palaeozoic</a> - before about 380 to 300&#160;million years ago - and, in places, were <a href="/wiki/Metamorphism_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metamorphism (geology)">metamorphosed</a> under high pressure and temperature or were crystallized by ascending <a href="/wiki/Magma" title="Magma">magma</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Earth%27s_crust" class="mw-redirect" title="Earth's crust">Earth's crust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-geobavaria_S4_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geobavaria_S4-28">[28]</a></sup> Rocks which were unchanged or only lightly metamorphosed, because they had been deformed at shallow crustal depths, include the <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_(geology)" title="Mississippian (geology)">Lower Carboniferous</a> shale and greywacke of Franconian Forest. The Fichtel mountains, the Münchberg Plateau and the Spessart, by contrast, have more metamorphic rocks (<a href="/wiki/Phyllite" title="Phyllite">phyllite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schist" title="Schist">schist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amphibolite" title="Amphibolite">amphibolite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gneiss" title="Gneiss">gneiss</a>). The Fichtel mountains are also characterized by large <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> bodies, called post-kinematic <a href="/wiki/Pluton_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pluton (geology)">plutons</a> which, in the late phase of Variscan orogeny, intruded into the metamorphic rocks. In most cases these are S-type granites whose melting was caused by heated-up sedimentary rocks sunk deep into the Earth's crust.<sup id="cite_ref-geobavaria_S24_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geobavaria_S24-29">[29]</a></sup> While the Fichtel and Franconian Forest can be assigned to the Saxo-Thuringian Zone of Central European Variscan orogeny, the Spessart belongs to the Central German Crystalline Zone.<sup id="cite_ref-geobavaria_S4_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geobavaria_S4-28">[28]</a></sup> The Münchberg mass is variously attributed to the Saxo-Thuringian or Moldanubian Zones.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>A substantially larger part of the shallow subsurface in Franconia comprises <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic" title="Mesozoic">Mesozoic</a>, unmetamorphosed, unfolded rocks of the <a href="/wiki/South_German_Scarplands" title="South German Scarplands">South German Scarplands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-geobavaria_S26_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geobavaria_S26-31">[31]</a></sup> The regional geological element of the South German Scarplands is the Franconian Platform (<i>Süddeutsche Großscholle</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> At the so-called <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Line" title="Franconian Line">Franconian Line</a>, a significant <a href="/wiki/Fault_(geology)" title="Fault (geology)">fault line</a>, the Saxo-Thuringian-Moldanubian basement was uplifted in places up to 2000&#160;m above the Franconian Platform.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The western two-thirds of Franconia is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siltstone" title="Siltstone">siltstones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Claystone" class="mw-redirect" title="Claystone">claystones</a> (so-called <a href="/wiki/Siliciclastic" title="Siliciclastic">siliciclastics</a>) of the <a href="/wiki/Bunter_sandstone" class="mw-redirect" title="Bunter sandstone">bunter sandstone</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marl" title="Marl">marls</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Muschelkalk" title="Muschelkalk">Muschelkalk</a> and the mixed, but predominantly siliciclastic, sedimentary rocks of the <a href="/wiki/Keuper" title="Keuper">Keuper</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B6n" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhön">Rhön</a>, the Triassic rocks are overlain and intruded by <a href="/wiki/Vulcanite" title="Vulcanite">volcanic rock</a> (<a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basanite_(rocks)" class="mw-redirect" title="Basanite (rocks)">basanites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phonolite" title="Phonolite">phonolites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trachyte" title="Trachyte">trachytes</a>) of the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary" title="Tertiary">Tertiary</a>. The eastern third of Franconia is dominated by the Jurassic rocks of the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Jura" title="Franconian Jura">Franconian Jura</a>, with the dark shales of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Jura" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Jura">Black Jura</a>, the shales and ferruginous sandstones of the <a href="/wiki/Brown_Jura" class="mw-redirect" title="Brown Jura">Brown Jura</a> and, the weathering-resistant limestones and <a href="/wiki/Dolomite_(rocks)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dolomite (rocks)">dolomitic rocks</a> of the <a href="/wiki/White_Jura" class="mw-redirect" title="White Jura">White Jura</a>, which stand out from the landscape and form the actual ridge of the Franconian Jura itself.<sup id="cite_ref-geobavaria_S26_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geobavaria_S26-31">[31]</a></sup> In the Jura, mostly siliciclastic sedimentary rocks formed in the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cretaceous (geology)">Cretaceous</a> have survived.</p>
<p>The Mesozoic sediments have been deposited in largescale basin areas. During the Triassic, the Franconian part of these depressions was often part of the mainland, in the Jurassic it was covered for most of the time by a <a href="/wiki/Marginal_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Marginal sea">marginal sea</a> of the western <a href="/wiki/Tethys_(ocean)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tethys (ocean)">Tethys Ocean</a>. At the time when the limestones and dolomites of the White Jura were being deposited, this sea was divided into sponge reefs and intervening lagoons. The reef bodies and the fine-grained lagoon limestones and marls are the material from which the majority of the Franconian Jura is composed today.<sup id="cite_ref-geobavaria_S40ff_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geobavaria_S40ff-34">[34]</a></sup> Following a drop in the sea level towards the end of the Upper Jurassic, larger areas also became part of the mainland at the beginning of the subsequent Cretaceous period. During the Upper Cretaceous, the sea advanced again up to the area of the Franconian Jura. At the end of the Cretaceous, the sea then retreated again from the region.<sup id="cite_ref-geobavaria_S40ff_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geobavaria_S40ff-34">[34]</a></sup> In addition, large parts of South and Central Germany experienced a general uplift -or in areas where the basement had broken through a substantial uplift - the course of formation of the Alps during the Tertiary. Since then, Franconia has been mainly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Erosion_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Erosion (geology)">erosion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weathering" title="Weathering">weathering</a> (especially in the Jura in the form of <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a>), which has ultimately led to formation of today's landscapes.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fossils">Fossils</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fossils">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plateosaurus_skull.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Plateosaurus_skull.jpg/220px-Plateosaurus_skull.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Plateosaurus_skull.jpg/330px-Plateosaurus_skull.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Plateosaurus_skull.jpg/440px-Plateosaurus_skull.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plateosaurus_skull.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skull and forward cervical spine of <i>Plateosaurus engelhardti</i>, probably the replica of a skeleton from <a href="/wiki/Ellingen" title="Ellingen">Ellingen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Archaeopteryx_lithographica,_replica_of_London_specimen,_Staatliches_Museum_f%C3%BCr_Naturkunde_Karlsruhe,_Germany_-_20100925.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Archaeopteryx_lithographica%2C_replica_of_London_specimen%2C_Staatliches_Museum_f%C3%BCr_Naturkunde_Karlsruhe%2C_Germany_-_20100925.jpg/170px-Archaeopteryx_lithographica%2C_replica_of_London_specimen%2C_Staatliches_Museum_f%C3%BCr_Naturkunde_Karlsruhe%2C_Germany_-_20100925.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Archaeopteryx_lithographica%2C_replica_of_London_specimen%2C_Staatliches_Museum_f%C3%BCr_Naturkunde_Karlsruhe%2C_Germany_-_20100925.jpg/255px-Archaeopteryx_lithographica%2C_replica_of_London_specimen%2C_Staatliches_Museum_f%C3%BCr_Naturkunde_Karlsruhe%2C_Germany_-_20100925.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Archaeopteryx_lithographica%2C_replica_of_London_specimen%2C_Staatliches_Museum_f%C3%BCr_Naturkunde_Karlsruhe%2C_Germany_-_20100925.jpg/340px-Archaeopteryx_lithographica%2C_replica_of_London_specimen%2C_Staatliches_Museum_f%C3%BCr_Naturkunde_Karlsruhe%2C_Germany_-_20100925.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4208" data-file-height="5625" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Archaeopteryx_lithographica,_replica_of_London_specimen,_Staatliches_Museum_f%C3%BCr_Naturkunde_Karlsruhe,_Germany_-_20100925.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The so-called London Exemplar of <i>Archaeopteryx</i> (here a replica) comes from the <a href="/wiki/Langenaltheim" title="Langenaltheim">Langenaltheim</a> Quarry, west of Solnhofen.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The oldest <a href="/wiki/Macrofossil" title="Macrofossil">macrofossils</a> in Franconia, which are also the oldest in Bavaria, are <a href="/wiki/Archaeocyatha" title="Archaeocyatha">archaeocyatha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sponge" title="Sponge">sponge</a>-like, goblet-shaped marine organisms, which were discovered in 2013 in a limestone block of <a href="/wiki/Cambrian" title="Cambrian">Late Lower Cambrian</a> age, about 520&#160;million years old. The block comes from the vicinity <a href="/wiki/Schwarzenbach_am_Wald" title="Schwarzenbach am Wald">Schwarzenbach am Wald</a> from the so-called Heinersreuth Block Conglomerate (<i>Heinersreuther Blockkonglomerat</i>), a <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_(geology)" title="Mississippian (geology)">Lower Carboniferous</a> <a href="/wiki/Wildflysch" class="mw-redirect" title="Wildflysch">wildflysch</a>. However, the aforementioned archaeocyathids are not three-dimensional fossils, but two-dimensional <a href="/wiki/Thin_section" title="Thin section">thin sections</a>. These thin sections had already been prepared and investigated in the 1970s but the archaeocyathids among them were apparently overlooked at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Better known and more highly respected fossil finds in Franconia come from the unfolded sedimentary rocks of the Triassic and Jurassic. The <a href="/wiki/Bunter_sandstone" class="mw-redirect" title="Bunter sandstone">bunter sandstone</a>, however, only has a relatively small number of preserved whole fossils. Much more commonly, it contains <a href="/wiki/Trace_fossil" title="Trace fossil">trace fossils</a>, especially the <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapod</a> footprints of <i><a href="/wiki/Chirotherium" title="Chirotherium">Chirotherium</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Type_locality_(biology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Type locality (biology)">type locality</a> for these <a href="/wiki/Animal_track" title="Animal track">animal tracks</a> is <a href="/wiki/Hildburghausen" title="Hildburghausen">Hildburghausen</a> in the Thuringian part of Franconia, where it occurs in the so-called Thuringian Chirotherium Sandstone (<i>Thüringer Chirotheriensandstein</i>, main Middle Bunter Sandstone).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> <i>Chirotherium</i> is also found in the Bavarian and Württemberg parts of Franconia. Sites include <a href="/wiki/Aura_an_der_Saale" title="Aura an der Saale">Aura</a> near Bad Kissingen, <a href="/wiki/Karbach_(Lower_Franconia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Karbach (Lower Franconia)">Karbach</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gambach_(Karlstadt)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gambach (Karlstadt) (page does not exist)">Gambach</a> and <a href="/wiki/K%C3%BClsheim" title="Külsheim">Külsheim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-haderer95_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haderer95-37">[37]</a></sup> There the deposits are somewhat younger (Upper Bunter Sandstone), and the corresponding <a href="/wiki/Stratigraphy_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stratigraphy (geology)">stratigraphic</a> interval is called the Franconian Chirotherium Beds (<i>Fränkische Chirotherienschichten</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-haderer95_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haderer95-37">[37]</a></sup> Among the less significant body fossil records of vertebrates are the <a href="/wiki/Procolophonoidea" title="Procolophonoidea">procolophonid</a> <i>Anomoiodon liliensterni</i> from <a href="/wiki/Reurieth" title="Reurieth">Reurieth</a> in the Thuringian part of Franconia<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and <i>Koiloskiosaurus coburgiensis</i> from <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6dental" title="Rödental">Mittelberg</a> near Coburg,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> both from the Thuringian Chirotherium Sandstone, and the <a href="/wiki/Temnospondyli" title="Temnospondyli">Temnospondyle</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Mastodonsaurus" title="Mastodonsaurus">Mastodonsaurus ingens</a></i> (possibly identical with the mastodonsaurus, <i><a href="/wiki/Heptasaurus_cappelensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Heptasaurus cappelensis">Heptasaurus cappelensis</a></i>) from the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6t_Formation" title="Röt Formation">Upper Bunter</a> at Gambach.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>As early as the first decade of the 19th century <a href="/wiki/George,_Count_of_M%C3%BCnster" class="mw-redirect" title="George, Count of Münster">George, Count of Münster</a> began systematic fossil gathering and digs and in the Upper <a href="/wiki/Muschelkalk" title="Muschelkalk">Muschelkalk</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bayreuth" title="Bayreuth">Bayreuth</a>. For example, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Oschenberg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oschenberg (page does not exist)">Oschenberg</a> hill near <a href="/w/index.php?title=Laineck&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Laineck (page does not exist)">Laineck</a> became the type locality of two relatively well-known marine reptiles of the Triassic period, later found in other parts of Central Europe: the "flat tooth lizard", <i><a href="/wiki/Placodus" title="Placodus">Placodus</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and the "false lizard", <i><a href="/wiki/Nothosaurus" title="Nothosaurus">Nothosaurus</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Franconia's middle <a href="/wiki/Keuper" title="Keuper">Keuper</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Feuerletten" class="mw-redirect" title="Feuerletten">Feuerletten</a>) is one of the best known and most common species of dinosaurs of Central Europe: <i><a href="/wiki/Plateosaurus_engelhardti" class="mw-redirect" title="Plateosaurus engelhardti">Plateosaurus engelhardti</a></i>, an early representative of the <a href="/wiki/Sauropodomorpha" title="Sauropodomorpha">sauropodomorpha</a>. Its type locality is located at <a href="/wiki/Heroldsberg" title="Heroldsberg">Heroldsberg</a> south of Nuremberg. When the remains of <i>Plateosaurus</i> were first discovered there in 1834, it was the first discovery of a dinosaur on German soil, and this occurred even before the name "dinosauria" was coined. Another important <i>Plateosaurus</i> find in Franconia was made at <a href="/wiki/Ellingen" title="Ellingen">Ellingen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Far more famous than <i>Plateosaurus</i>, <i>Placodus</i> and <i>Nothosaurus</i> is the <i><a href="/wiki/Archaeopteryx" title="Archaeopteryx">Archaeopteryx</a></i>, probably the first bird geologically. It was discovered in the southern Franconian Jura, <i>inter alia</i> at the famous fossil site of Solnhofen in the Solnhofen Platform Limestone (<i>Solnhofener Plattenkalk</i>, (Solnhofen-Formation, early <a href="/wiki/Tithonian" title="Tithonian">Tithonian</a>, Upper Jurassic). In addition to <i>Archaeopteryx</i>, in the very fine-grained, laminated lagoon limestones are the pterosaur <i><a href="/wiki/Pterodactylus" title="Pterodactylus">Pterodactylus</a></i> and various <a href="/wiki/Bony_fish" class="mw-redirect" title="Bony fish">bony fishes</a> as well as numerous extremely detailed examples of invertebrates e.g. <a href="/wiki/Feather_star" class="mw-redirect" title="Feather star">feather stars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dragonflies" class="mw-redirect" title="Dragonflies">dragonflies</a>. <a href="/wiki/Eichst%C3%A4tt" title="Eichstätt">Eichstätt</a> is the other "big" and similarly famous fossil locality in the Solnhofen Formation, situated on the southern edge of the Jura in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">Upper Bavaria</a>. Here, as well as <i>Archaeopteryx</i>, the theropod dinosaurs, <i><a href="/wiki/Compsognathus" title="Compsognathus">Compsognathus</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Juravenator" title="Juravenator">Juravenator</a>,</i> were found.</p>
<p>An inglorious episode in the history of paleontology took place in Franconia: fake fossils, known as <a href="/wiki/Beringer%27s_Lying_Stones" title="Beringer's Lying Stones">Beringer's Lying Stones</a>, were acquired in the 1720s by Würzburg doctor and naturalist, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Beringer" class="mw-redirect" title="Johann Beringer">Johann Beringer</a>, for a lot of money and then described in a <a href="/wiki/Monograph" title="Monograph">monograph</a>, along with genuine fossils from the Würzburg area. However, it is not entirely clear whether the Beringer forgeries were actually planted or whether he himself was responsible for the fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Franconia has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid</a> <a href="/wiki/Cool_temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Cool temperate">cool temperate</a> transitional climate, which is neither very continental nor very maritime. The average monthly temperatures vary depending on the area between about -1 to -2&#160;°C in January and 17 to 19&#160;°C in August, but may reach a peak of about 35&#160;°C for a few days in the summer, especially in the large cities. The climate of Franconia is sunny and relatively warm. For part of the summer, for example, Lower Franconia is one the sunniest areas in Germany. Daily temperatures in the Bavarian part of Franconia are an average of 0.1&#160;°C higher than the average for Bavaria as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Relatively less rain falls in Franconia, and likewise in the rest of North Bavaria rain than is usual for its geographic location; even summer storms are often less powerful than in other areas of South Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In southern Bavaria about 2,000&#160;mm of precipitation falls annually and almost three times as much as in parts of Franconia (about 500–900&#160;mm) in the rain shadow of the Spessart, Rhön and Odenwald.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quality_of_life">Quality of life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Quality of life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Franconia, as part of Germany, has a high <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>. In the <i>Worldwide Quality of Living Survey</i> by <a href="/wiki/Mercer_(consulting_firm)" title="Mercer (consulting firm)">Mercer</a> in 2010, the city of Nuremberg was one of the top 25 cities in the world in terms of quality of life and came sixth in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-mercer_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mercer-49">[49]</a></sup> In environmental ranking Nuremberg came thirteenth in the world and was the best German city<sup id="cite_ref-mercer_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mercer-49">[49]</a></sup> In a survey by the German magazine, <i><a href="/wiki/Focus_(German_magazine)" title="Focus (German magazine)">Focus</a>,</i> on quality of life in 2014, the districts of Eichstätt and Fürth were among the top positions in the table.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> In the <i>Glücksatlas</i> by <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Post_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Deutsche Post AG">Deutsche Post</a> Franconia achieved some of the highest scores,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> but the region slipped in 2013 to 13th place out of 19.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Franconia" title="History of Franconia">History of Franconia</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Franconia is named after the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribe</a> who conquered most of Western Europe by the middle of the 8th century. Despite its name, Franconia is not the homeland of the Franks, but rather owes its name to being partially settled by Franks from the Rhineland during the <a href="/wiki/7th_century_AD" class="mw-redirect" title="7th century AD">7th century AD</a> following the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Alamanni" class="mw-redirect" title="Alamanni">Alamanni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thuringians" class="mw-redirect" title="Thuringians">Thuringians</a> who had dominated the region earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of the 10th century a <i>Duchy of Franconia</i> (German: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Herzogtum Franken</i></span>) was established within <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a>, which comprised modern <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palatinate_(region)" title="Palatinate (region)">Palatinate</a>, parts of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a> and most of today's Franconia. After the dissolution of the so-called <a href="/wiki/Stem_duchy" title="Stem duchy">Stem duchy</a> of Franconia, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Emperors</a> created the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Circle" title="Franconian Circle">Franconian Circle</a> (German <i>Fränkischer Reichskreis</i>) in 1500 to embrace the principalities that grew out of the eastern half of the former duchy. The territory of the Franconian Circle roughly corresponds with modern Franconia. The title of a <i>Duke of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Franconia" title="Duchy of Franconia">Franconia</a></i> was claimed by the <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Bishopric of Würzburg">Würzburg bishops</a> until 1803 and by the kings of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">Bavaria</a> until 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Examples of Franconian cities founded by Frankish noblemen are <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>, first mentioned in the 7th century, <a href="/wiki/Ansbach" title="Ansbach">Ansbach</a>, first mentioned in 748, and <a href="/wiki/Wei%C3%9Fenburg_in_Bayern" title="Weißenburg in Bayern">Weissenburg</a>, founded in the 7th century.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history_and_Antiquity">Early history and Antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Early history and Antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Staffelberg_2006-05-07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Staffelberg_2006-05-07.jpg/220px-Staffelberg_2006-05-07.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Staffelberg_2006-05-07.jpg/330px-Staffelberg_2006-05-07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Staffelberg_2006-05-07.jpg/440px-Staffelberg_2006-05-07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Staffelberg_2006-05-07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> built the mighty fortress of <a href="/wiki/Menosgada" title="Menosgada">Menosgada</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Staffelberg" title="Staffelberg">Staffelberg</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Fossil finds show that the region was already settled by <a href="/wiki/Caveman" title="Caveman">primitive man</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i>, in the middle <a href="/wiki/Ice_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Ice Age">Ice Age</a> about 600,000&#160;years ago. Probably the oldest human remains in the Bavarian part of Franconia were found in the cave ruins of Hunas at <a href="/wiki/Pommelsbrunn" title="Pommelsbrunn">Pommelsbrunn</a> in the county of <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Land" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg Land">Nuremberg Land</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In the late <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, the region was probably only sparsely inhabited, as few <a href="/wiki/Noble_metal" title="Noble metal">noble metals</a> occur here and the soils are only moderately fertile.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> (from about 800&#160;B.C.) the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> become the first nation to be discernible in the region. In northern Franconia they built a chain of <a href="/wiki/Hill_fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Hill fort">hill forts</a> as a line of defence against the <a href="/wiki/Germanii" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanii">Germanii</a> advancing from the north. On the <a href="/wiki/Staffelberg" title="Staffelberg">Staffelberg</a> they built a powerful settlement, to which <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> the name <i><a href="/wiki/Menosgada" title="Menosgada">oppidum Menosgada</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and on the <a href="/wiki/Gleichberge" title="Gleichberge">Gleichberge</a> is the largest surviving <i><a href="/wiki/Oppidum" title="Oppidum">oppidum</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Germany_(geography)" title="Central Germany (geography)">Central Germany</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Oppidum_Steinsburg" title="Oppidum Steinsburg">Steinsburg</a>. With the increased expansion of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Rome</a> in the first century B.C. and the simultaneous advance of the <a href="/wiki/Elbe_Germanii" class="mw-redirect" title="Elbe Germanii">Elbe Germanic tribes</a> from the north, the Celtic culture begain to fall into decline. The southern parts of present-day Franconia soon fell under Roman control; however, most of the region remained in <a href="/wiki/Free_Germania" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Germania">Free Germania</a>. Initially Rome tried extend its direct influence far to the northeast; in the longer term, however, the Germanic-Roman frontier formed further southwest.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wei%C3%9Fenburg_Porta_decumana1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Wei%C3%9Fenburg_Porta_decumana1.jpg/220px-Wei%C3%9Fenburg_Porta_decumana1.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Wei%C3%9Fenburg_Porta_decumana1.jpg/330px-Wei%C3%9Fenburg_Porta_decumana1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Wei%C3%9Fenburg_Porta_decumana1.jpg/440px-Wei%C3%9Fenburg_Porta_decumana1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2268" data-file-height="1527" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wei%C3%9Fenburg_Porta_decumana1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A 1990 replica of the <i>Porta decumana</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Biriciana" title="Biriciana">Biriciana</a>. View over the camp ring road</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under the emperors, <a href="/wiki/Domitian" title="Domitian">Domitian</a> (81-96), <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">Trajan</a> (98-117) and <a href="/wiki/Hadrian_(emperor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadrian (emperor)">Hadrian</a> (117-138), the <a href="/wiki/Rhaetian_Limes" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhaetian Limes">Rhaetian Limes</a> was built as a border facing the Germanic tribes to the north. This defensive line ran through the south of Franconia and described an arc across the region whose northernmost point lay at present-day <a href="/wiki/Gunzenhausen" title="Gunzenhausen">Gunzenhausen</a>. To protect it, the Romans built several forts like <a href="/wiki/Biriciana" title="Biriciana">Biriciana</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wei%C3%9Fenburg_in_Bayern" title="Weißenburg in Bayern">Weißenburg</a>, but by the mid-third century, the border could no longer be maintained and by 250&#160;A.D. the <a href="/wiki/Alemanni" title="Alemanni">Alemanni</a> occupied the areas up to the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>. Fortified settlements such as the <a href="/wiki/Gelbe_B%C3%BCrg" class="mw-redirect" title="Gelbe Bürg">Gelbe Bürg</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dittenheim" title="Dittenheim">Dittenheim</a> controlled the new areas.<sup id="cite_ref-kraus2_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kraus2-60">[60]</a></sup> More such Gau forts have been detected north of the former Limes as well. To which tribe their occupants belonged is unknown in most cases. However, it is likely that it was mainly Alemanni and <a href="/wiki/Juthungi" title="Juthungi">Juthungi</a> in especially in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-Kraus1_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kraus1-61">[61]</a></sup> By contrast, it was the <a href="/wiki/Burgundians" title="Burgundians">Burgundians</a> who settled on the Lower and Middle Main.<sup id="cite_ref-Kraus1_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kraus1-61">[61]</a></sup> Many of these hill forts appear to have been destroyed, however, no later than 500&#160;A.D. The reasons are not entirely clear, but it could have been as a result of invasions by the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a> which thus triggered the <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">Great Migration</a>. In many cases, however, it was probably conquest by the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a> that spelt the end of these hilltop settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-kraus2_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kraus2-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grave_Westheim.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Grave_Westheim.JPG/220px-Grave_Westheim.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Grave_Westheim.JPG/330px-Grave_Westheim.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Grave_Westheim.JPG/440px-Grave_Westheim.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grave_Westheim.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Franconian warrior's grave goods from the early mediaeval burial site of <a href="/wiki/Westheim_(Mittelfranken)" class="mw-redirect" title="Westheim (Mittelfranken)">Westheim</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franken-um-800.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Franken-um-800.jpg/220px-Franken-um-800.jpg" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Franken-um-800.jpg/330px-Franken-um-800.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Franken-um-800.jpg/440px-Franken-um-800.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1344" data-file-height="1280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franken-um-800.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Duchy of Franconia around 800</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With their victories over the heartlands of the Alamanni and <a href="/wiki/Thuringians" class="mw-redirect" title="Thuringians">Thuringians</a> in the 6th century, the present region of Franconia also fell to the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-francia_orientalis_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-francia_orientalis-2">[2]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Division_of_the_Frankish_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Division of the Frankish Empire">division of the Frankish Empire</a>, East Francia (<i>Francia orientialis</i>) was formed from the territories of the dioceses of <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worms" class="mw-redirect" title="Worms">Worms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wurzburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Wurzburg">Wurzburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Speyer" title="Speyer">Speyer</a>. Later, the diocese of Bamberg was added.<sup id="cite_ref-francia_orientalis_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-francia_orientalis-2">[2]</a></sup> In the 7th century, the <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> started to populate the northeastern parts of the region from the east, because the area of today's Upper Franconia was very sparsely populated (<a href="/wiki/Bavaria_Slavica" title="Bavaria Slavica">Bavaria Slavica</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-slawen_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slawen-62">[62]</a></sup> However, in the 10th and 11th centuries, they largely gave up their own language and cultural tradition. The majority of the population of Franconia was <a href="/wiki/Pagan" class="mw-redirect" title="Pagan">pagan</a> well into the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a>, The first people to spread the Christian faith strongly were wandering <a href="/wiki/Ireland_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ireland (island)">Irish</a> <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon">Anglo-Saxon</a> <a href="/wiki/Monk" title="Monk">monks</a> in the early 7th century. <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kilian" title="Saint Kilian">Saint Kilian</a>, who together with his companions, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Colman_(martyr)" title="Saint Colman (martyr)">Saint Colman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Totnan" title="Saint Totnan">Saint Totnan</a> are considered to be the <a href="/wiki/Apostle" title="Apostle">apostles</a> to the Franks, suffering martyrdom in Würzburg in the late 7th century, probably did not encounter any pagans in the ducal court. It was probably <a href="/wiki/Saint_Boniface" title="Saint Boniface">Saint Boniface</a> who carried the Christian mission deep into the heart of the ordinary population of Franconia.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Franconia" title="Duchy of Franconia">Duchy of Franconia</a></div>
<p>In the mid-9th century the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Franconia" title="Duchy of Franconia">tribal Duchy of Franconia</a> emerged, one of the five tribal or <a href="/wiki/Stem_duchies" class="mw-redirect" title="Stem duchies">stem duchies</a> of <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hdbg3_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdbg3-64">[64]</a></sup> The territory of the stem duchy was far bigger than modern Franconia and covered the whole of present-day Hesse, northern Baden-Württemberg, southern Thuringia, large parts of Rhineland-Palatinate and parts of the Franconian provinces in Bavaria. It extended as far west as <a href="/wiki/Speyer" title="Speyer">Speyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Worms,_Germany" title="Worms, Germany">Worms</a> (west of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>) and even included <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> ("ford of the Franks"). In the early 10th century, the <a href="/wiki/Babenbergs" class="mw-redirect" title="Babenbergs">Babenbergs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conradines" title="Conradines">Conradines</a> fought for power in Franconia. Ultimately this discord led to the <a href="/wiki/Babenberg_Feud" class="mw-redirect" title="Babenberg Feud">Babenberg Feud</a> which was fuelled and controlled by the crown. The outcome of this feud meant the loss of power for the Babenbergs, but indirectly resulted in the Conradines winning the crown of East Francia. Sometime around 906, <a href="/wiki/Conrad_I_of_Germany" title="Conrad I of Germany">Conrad</a> succeeded in establishing his ducal hegemony over Franconia, but when the direct Carolingian male line failed in 911, Conrad was acclaimed <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_Kings_and_Emperors" class="mw-redirect" title="List of German Kings and Emperors">King of the Germans</a>, largely because of his weak position in his own duchy. Franconia, like <a href="/wiki/Alamannia" title="Alamannia">Alamannia</a> was fairly fragmented and the duke's position was often disputed between the chief families. Conrad had granted Franconia to his brother <a href="/wiki/Eberhard_of_Franconia" title="Eberhard of Franconia">Eberhard</a> on his succession, but when Eberhard rebelled against <a href="/wiki/Otto_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto I, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto I</a> in 938, he was deposed from his duchy, which disintegrated in 939 on Eberhard's death into West or <a href="/wiki/Rhenish_Franconia" title="Rhenish Franconia">Rhenish Franconia</a> (<i><span lang="la" xml:lang="la">Francia Rhenensis</span></i>), and East Franconia (<i><span lang="la" xml:lang="la">Francia Orientalis</span></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[note 1]</a></sup> and was directly subordinated to the Reich. Only after that was the former <i>Francia orientalis</i> considered to be under the sphere of the bishops of Würzburg as the true Franconia, its territory gradually shrinking to its present area.<sup id="cite_ref-francia_orientalis_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-francia_orientalis-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, the inhabitants of parts of present-day Upper and Middle Franconia, who were not under the control of Würzburg, probably also considered themselves to be Franks at that time, and certainly their dialect distinguished them from the inhabitants of Bavaria and <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-francia_orientalis2_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-francia_orientalis2-66">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike the other stem duchies, Franconia became the homeland and power base of East Frankish and German kings after the <a href="/wiki/Ottonians" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottonians">Ottonians</a> died out in 1024.<sup id="cite_ref-hdbg3_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdbg3-64">[64]</a></sup> As a result, in the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a>, the region did not become a strong regional force such as those which formed in Saxony, Bavaria and <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabia</a>. In 1007, the later canonized Henry II founded the <a href="/wiki/Arcbishopric_of_Bamberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Arcbishopric of Bamberg">Bishopric of Bamberg</a> and endowed it with rich estates.<sup id="cite_ref-bamberg_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bamberg-67">[66]</a></sup> Bamberg became a favoured <i><a href="/wiki/Kaiserpfalz" title="Kaiserpfalz">Pfalz</a></i> and an important centre of the Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-bamberg_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bamberg-67">[66]</a></sup> Because parts of the Bishopric of Würzburg also fell to Bamberg, Würzburg was enfeoffed several royal estates by King Henry II by way of compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franken_um_1250.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Franken_um_1250.jpg/220px-Franken_um_1250.jpg" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Franken_um_1250.jpg/330px-Franken_um_1250.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Franken_um_1250.jpg/440px-Franken_um_1250.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1777" data-file-height="1509" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franken_um_1250.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Franconia around 1200</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the 12th century <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Castle" title="Nuremberg Castle">Nuremberg Castle</a> was the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Burgraviate_of_Nuremberg" title="Burgraviate of Nuremberg">Burgraviate of Nuremberg</a>. The burgraviate was ruled from about 1190 by the Zollerns, the Franconian line of the later <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hohenzollern" title="House of Hohenzollern">House of Hohenzollern</a>, which provided the German emperors of the 19th and 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-burgn.C3.BCrnberg_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burgn.C3.BCrnberg-69">[68]</a></sup> Under the Hohenstaufen kings, <a href="/wiki/Conrad_III_(HRR)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conrad III (HRR)">Conrad&#160;III</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_(HRR)" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick I (HRR)">Frederick Barbarossa</a>, Franconia became the centre of power in the Empire. During the time when there was no emperor, the <a href="/wiki/Interregnum_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Interregnum (Holy Roman Empire)">Interregnum</a> (1254-1273), some <a href="/wiki/Territorial_prince" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial prince">territorial princes</a> became ever more powerful. After the Interregnum, however, the rulers succeeded in re-establishing a stronger royal lordship in Franconia.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> Franconia soon played an important role again for the monarchy at the time of <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_I_(HRR)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rudolf I (HRR)">Rudolf of Habsburg</a>; the itineraries of his successors showing their preference for the Rhine-Main region. In 1376 the <a href="/wiki/Swabian_League_of_Cities" title="Swabian League of Cities">Swabian League of Cities</a> was founded and was joined later by several Franconian <a href="/wiki/Imperial_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial cities">imperial cities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> During the 13th&#160;century the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Order" title="Teutonic Order">Teutonic Order</a> was formed, taking over its first possession in Franconia in 1209, the Bailiwick of Franconia. The foundation of many schools and hospitals and the construction of numerous churches and castles in this area goes back to the work of this Roman Catholic military order. The residence place of the bailiwick was at <a href="/wiki/Ellingen" title="Ellingen">Ellingen</a> until 1789 when it was transferred to today's <a href="/wiki/Bad_Mergentheim" title="Bad Mergentheim">Bad Mergentheim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kraus9_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kraus9-72">[71]</a></sup> Other orders such as the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar" title="Knights Templar">Knights Templar</a> could not gain a foothold in Franconia; the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_St._John" class="mw-redirect" title="Order of St. John">Order of St. John</a> worked in the Bishopric of Würzburg and had short term commands.<sup id="cite_ref-orden_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orden-73">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Successor_states_of_East_Francia">Successor states of East Francia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Successor states of East Francia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of the 13th century, the following states, among others, had formed in the territory of the former Duchy:</p>

<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_of_Abenberg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="County of Abenberg (page does not exist)">County of Abenberg</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_Period">Modern Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Modern Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Modern_Period">Early Modern Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Early Modern Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dankaerts-Historis-9308_-_Franconia_map.tiff" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Dankaerts-Historis-9308_-_Franconia_map.tiff/lossy-page1-220px-Dankaerts-Historis-9308_-_Franconia_map.tiff.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Dankaerts-Historis-9308_-_Franconia_map.tiff/lossy-page1-330px-Dankaerts-Historis-9308_-_Franconia_map.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Dankaerts-Historis-9308_-_Franconia_map.tiff/lossy-page1-440px-Dankaerts-Historis-9308_-_Franconia_map.tiff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4488" data-file-height="3582" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dankaerts-Historis-9308_-_Franconia_map.tiff" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Franconia, 1642</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 2&#160;July 1500 during the reign of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_(HRR)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximilian I (HRR)">Maximilian&#160;I</a>, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Reform_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Reform (Holy Roman Empire)">Imperial Reform Movement</a>, the Empire was divided into <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Circle" title="Imperial Circle">Imperial Circles</a>. This led in 1512 to the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Circle" title="Franconian Circle">Franconian Circle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-reichskreis2_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reichskreis2-3">[3]</a></sup> Seen from a modern perspective, the Franconian Circle may be viewed as an important basis for the sense of a common Franconian identity that exists today.<sup id="cite_ref-reichskreis3_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reichskreis3-11">[11]</a></sup> The Franconian Circle also shaped the geographical limits of the present-day Franconia.<sup id="cite_ref-francia_orientalis2_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-francia_orientalis2-66">[65]</a></sup> In the late Middle Ages and Early Modern Period, the Imperial Circle was severely affected by <i><a href="/wiki/Kleinstaaterei" title="Kleinstaaterei">Kleinstaaterei</a></i>, the patchwork of tiny states in this region of Germany. As during the late Middle Ages, the bishops of Würzburg used the nominal title of Duke of Franconia during the time of the Imperial Circle.<sup id="cite_ref-herzogfranken_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herzogfranken-74">[73]</a></sup> In 1559, the Franconian Circle was given jurisdiction over coinage (<i>Münzaufsicht</i>) and, in 1572, was the only Circle to issue its own police ordinance.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Members of the Franconian Circle included the imperial cities, the prince-bishoprics, the Bailiwick of Franconia of the Teutonic Order and several counties. The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Knight" title="Imperial Knight">Imperial Knights</a> with their tiny territories, of which there was a particularly large number in Franconia, were outside the Circle assembly and, until 1806, formed the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconian_Knights_Circle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Franconian Knights Circle (page does not exist)">Franconian Knights Circle</a> (<i>Fränkischer Ritterkreis</i>) consisting of six <a href="/wiki/Knights%27_Canton" class="mw-redirect" title="Knights' Canton">Knights' Cantons</a>. Because the extent of Franconia, already referred to above, is disputed, there were many areas that might be counted as part of Franconia today, that lay outside the Franconian Circle. For example, the area of Aschaffenburg belonged to <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Mainz">Electoral Mainz</a> and was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Rhenish_Circle" title="Electoral Rhenish Circle">Electoral Rhenish Circle</a>, the area of Coburg belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Saxon_Circle" title="Upper Saxon Circle">Upper Saxon Circle</a> and the Heilbronn area to the <a href="/wiki/Swabian_Circle" class="mw-redirect" title="Swabian Circle">Swabian Circle</a>. In the 16th century, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=College_of_Franconian_Counts&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="College of Franconian Counts (page does not exist)">College of Franconian Counts</a> was founded to represent the interests of the <a href="/wiki/Count" title="Count">counts</a> in Franconia.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Franconia played an important role in the spread of <a href="/wiki/The_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="The Reformation">the Reformation</a> initiated by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-kraus7_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kraus7-78">[77]</a></sup> Nuremberg being one of the places where the <a href="/wiki/Luther_Bible" title="Luther Bible">Luther Bible</a> was printed.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> The majority of other Franconian imperial cities and imperial knights embraced the new confession.<sup id="cite_ref-kraus6_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kraus6-80">[79]</a></sup> In the course of the <a href="/wiki/Counter-reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Counter-reformation">counter-reformation</a> several regions of Franconia returned to Catholicism, however, and there was also an increase in <a href="/wiki/Witch_trial" class="mw-redirect" title="Witch trial">witch trials</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> In addition to Lutheranism, the <a href="/wiki/Radical_Reformation" title="Radical Reformation">radical reformatory</a> <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">baptist</a> movement spread early on across the Franconian area. Important Baptist centres were <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsberg_in_Bayern" class="mw-redirect" title="Königsberg in Bayern">Königsberg</a> and Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Karte_bauernkrieg3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Karte_bauernkrieg3.jpg/220px-Karte_bauernkrieg3.jpg" width="220" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Karte_bauernkrieg3.jpg/330px-Karte_bauernkrieg3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Karte_bauernkrieg3.jpg/440px-Karte_bauernkrieg3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="922" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Karte_bauernkrieg3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Extent of the uprisings in the Peasants' War</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1525, the burden of heavy taxation and socage combined with new, liberal ideas that chimed with <a href="/wiki/The_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="The Reformation">the Reformation</a> movement, unleashed the <a href="/wiki/German_Peasants%27_War" title="German Peasants' War">German Peasants' War</a>. The Würzburg area was particularly hard hit with numerous castles and monasteries being burned down.<sup id="cite_ref-bauern_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauern-84">[83]</a></sup> In the end, however, the uprisings were suppressed and for centuries the lowest strata of society were excluded from all political activity.</p>
<p>From 1552, Margrave <a href="/wiki/Albert_Alcibiades" class="mw-redirect" title="Albert Alcibiades">Albert Alcibiades</a> attempted to break the supremacy of the mighty imperial city of Nuremberg and to secularise the ecclesial estates in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Margrave_War" title="Second Margrave War">Second Margrave War</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-kraus61_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kraus61-85">[84]</a></sup> to create a duchy over which he would rule.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> Large areas of Franconia were eventually devastated in the fighting until King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_(HRR)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinand I (HRR)">Ferdinand I</a> together with several dukes and princes decided to overthrow Albert.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Trexelplan_1632.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Trexelplan_1632.jpg/220px-Trexelplan_1632.jpg" width="220" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Trexelplan_1632.jpg/330px-Trexelplan_1632.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Trexelplan_1632.jpg/440px-Trexelplan_1632.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2552" data-file-height="3508" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Trexelplan_1632.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Part of Wallenstein's camp around <a href="/wiki/Zirndorf" title="Zirndorf">Zirndorf</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Alte_Veste" class="mw-redirect" title="Alte Veste">Alte Veste</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1608, the reformed princes merged into a so-called <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Union" title="Protestant Union">Union</a> within the Empire. In Franconia, the margraves of Ansbach and Bayreuth as well as the imperial cities were part of this alliance. The Catholic side responded in 1609 with a counter-alliance, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_League_(1609)" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic League (1609)">League</a>. The conflicts between the two camps ultimately resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, which was the greatest strain on the cohesion of the Franconian Circle<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> Initially, Franconia was not a theatre of war, although marauding armies repeatedly crossed its territory. However, in 1631, Swedish troops under <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_II_Adolphus_(Sweden)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gustavus II Adolphus (Sweden)">Gustavus Adolphus</a> advanced into Franconia and established a large encampment in summer 1632 around Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-kraus8_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kraus8-88">[87]</a></sup> However, the Swedes lost the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Alte_Veste" title="Battle of the Alte Veste">Battle of the Alte Veste</a> against <a href="/wiki/Wallenstein" class="mw-redirect" title="Wallenstein">Wallenstein</a>'s troops and eventually withdrew. Franconia was one of the poorest regions in the Empire and lost its imperial political significance.<sup id="cite_ref-hdbg1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdbg1-89">[88]</a></sup> During the course of the war, about half the local population lost their lives. To compensate for these losses about 150,000&#160;displaced Protestants settled in Protestant areas, including <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Exiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Exiles">exiles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fraenkischer_Reichskreis.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Fraenkischer_Reichskreis.png/220px-Fraenkischer_Reichskreis.png" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Fraenkischer_Reichskreis.png/330px-Fraenkischer_Reichskreis.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Fraenkischer_Reichskreis.png/440px-Fraenkischer_Reichskreis.png 2x" data-file-width="2360" data-file-height="1650" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fraenkischer_Reichskreis.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Franconian Imperial Circle in 1789</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Franconia never developed into a unified territorial state, because the patchwork quilt of small states (<i><a href="/wiki/Kleinstaaterei" title="Kleinstaaterei">Kleinstaaterei</a></i>) survived the Middle Ages and lasted until the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-hdbg2_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdbg2-91">[90]</a></sup> As a result, the Franconian Circle had the important task of preserving peace, preventing abuses and to repairing war damage and had a regulatory role in the region until the end of the Holy Roman Empire. Until the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, the Circle had become an almost independent organization and joined the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_(League_of_Augsburg)" title="Grand Alliance (League of Augsburg)">Grand Alliance</a> against <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a> as an almost sovereign state. The Circle also developed early forms of a <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hdbg2_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdbg2-91">[90]</a></sup> It also played a major role in the control of disease during the 16th and 17th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Charles_Alexander_(Brandenburg-Ansbach-Bayreuth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Alexander (Brandenburg-Ansbach-Bayreuth)">Charles Alexander</a> abdicated in 1792, the former margraviates of Ansbach and Bayreuth were annexed by <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-preu.C3.9Fen_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-preu.C3.9Fen-94">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Karl_August_Freiherr_von_Hardenberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Karl August Freiherr von Hardenberg">Karl August Freiherr von Hardenberg</a> was appointed as governor of these areas by Prussia.<sup id="cite_ref-preu.C3.9Fen_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-preu.C3.9Fen-94">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_Modern_Period">Later Modern Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Later Modern Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Most of modern-day Franconia became part of Bavaria in 1803 thanks to Bavaria's alliance with <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>. Culturally it is in many ways different from Bavaria proper ("Altbayern", Old Bavaria), however. The ancient name was resurrected in 1837 by <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_I_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig I of Bavaria">Ludwig I of Bavaria</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Nazi</a> period, Bavaria was broken up into several different <a href="/wiki/Gau_(country_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gau (country subdivision)">Gaue</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Gau_Franconia" title="Gau Franconia">Franconia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gau_Mainfranken" class="mw-redirect" title="Gau Mainfranken">Main-Franconia</a>.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In 1803, what was to become the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">Kingdom of Bavaria</a> was given large parts of Franconia through the enactment of the <i><a href="/wiki/Reichsdeputationshauptschluss" title="Reichsdeputationshauptschluss">Reichsdeputationshauptschluss</a></i> under pressure from <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> for <a href="/wiki/Secularization" title="Secularization">secularization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mediatisation" title="Mediatisation">mediatisation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> In 1806, the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Confederation" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Confederation">Act of Confederation</a> led to stronger ties between Bavaria, Württemberg, Baden and other areas with France, whereupon the Holy Roman Empire including the Franconian Circle fell apart.<sup id="cite_ref-rheinbundakte_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rheinbundakte-96">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> As a reward Bavaria was promised other estates, including the city of Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-rheinbundakte_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rheinbundakte-96">[95]</a></sup> In the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Rittersturm" title="Rittersturm">Rittersturm</a></i> of 1803, Bavaria, Württemberg and Baden seized the territories of the Imperial Knights and Franconian nobility, whoses estates were often no bigger than a few parishes, even though the <i>Reichsdeputationshauptschluss</i> had not authorised this.<sup id="cite_ref-herzogfranken_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herzogfranken-74">[73]</a></sup> In 1806 and 1810, Prussia had to release the territories of Ansbach and Bayreuth, which it had annexed in 1792, to Bavaria, whereby Prussia lost its supremacy in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-preu.C3.9Fen_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-preu.C3.9Fen-94">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1814, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>,the territories of the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Aschaffenburg" title="Principality of Aschaffenburg">Principality of Aschaffenburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Grand Duchy of Würzburg">Grand Duchy of Würzburg</a> went to the Kingdom of Bavaria. In order to merge the <a href="/wiki/Patchwork_quilt" title="Patchwork quilt">patchwork quilt</a> of small states in Franconia and Swabia into a greater Bavaria, <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Montgelas" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximilian Montgelas">Maximilian Joseph Montgelas</a> reformed the political structure.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> Out of this in January 1838 emerged the Franconian provinces with their present names of Middle, Upper and Lower Franconia. .<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Considerable resentment arose in parts of the Franconian territories over their new membership of Bavaria.<sup id="cite_ref-geschichte_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geschichte-101">[100]</a></sup> There were liberal demands for republican structures which erupted in the <a href="/wiki/German_Revolution_(1848/1849)" class="mw-redirect" title="German Revolution (1848/1849)">revolts of 1848 and 1849</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaibach_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gaibach Festival (page does not exist)">Gaibach Festival</a> in 1832.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> On the one hand the reconciliation policy of the <a href="/wiki/Wittelsbachs" class="mw-redirect" title="Wittelsbachs">Wittelsbachs</a><sup id="cite_ref-geschichte_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geschichte-101">[100]</a></sup> and Montgelas' aforementioned policy of unification, and, on the other hand, the inclusion of Bavaria in the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> in 1871, which weakened her power Bavaria slightly, the conflict between Franconia and Bavaria eased considerably.</p>
<p>From 1836 to 1846, the Kingdom of Bavaria built the <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Canal" title="Ludwig Canal">Ludwig Canal</a> from Bamberg to Kelheim, which was only abandoned in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> However, the canal lost much of its importance shortly after the arrival of the railways. Between 1843 and 1854, the <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_South-North_Railway" title="Ludwig South-North Railway">Ludwig South-North Railway</a> was established within Franconia, which ran from <a href="/wiki/Lindau_(Lake_Constance)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lindau (Lake Constance)">Lindau</a> on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Constance" title="Lake Constance">Lake Constance</a> via <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bamberg" title="Bamberg">Bamberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kulmbach" title="Kulmbach">Kulmbach</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hof_(Saale)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hof (Saale)">Hof</a>. The first locomotive to run on German soil steamed 1835 from Nuremberg to Fürth on 7 December 1835.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a> the monarchy in Bavaria was abolished, but the state could not agree on a compromise between a <a href="/wiki/Soviet_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet system">Soviet system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliamentarianism" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentarianism">parliamentarianism</a>. This caused fighting between the opposing camps and the then prime minister was shot. As a result, the government fled to Bamberg in 1919, where the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bamberg_Constitution&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bamberg Constitution (page does not exist)">Bamberg Constitution</a> was adopted while, in Munich, the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Soviet_Republic" title="Bavarian Soviet Republic">Bavarian Soviet Republic</a> reigned briefly.<sup id="cite_ref-bam-haupt_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bam-haupt-105">[104]</a></sup> In 1919 the <a href="/wiki/Free_State_of_Coburg" title="Free State of Coburg">Free State of Coburg</a> voted in a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> against joining <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a> and was instead united with Bavaria on 1&#160;July 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-bam-haupt_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bam-haupt-105">[104]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
