<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Karl_Emil_Otto_Fritsch-Denkmaeler_Deutscher_Renaissance-1891-Nuernberg-Pellerhaus_zu_Nuernberg_Aegidienplatz_1605_Facade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Karl_Emil_Otto_Fritsch-Denkmaeler_Deutscher_Renaissance-1891-Nuernberg-Pellerhaus_zu_Nuernberg_Aegidienplatz_1605_Facade.jpg/170px-Karl_Emil_Otto_Fritsch-Denkmaeler_Deutscher_Renaissance-1891-Nuernberg-Pellerhaus_zu_Nuernberg_Aegidienplatz_1605_Facade.jpg" width="170" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Karl_Emil_Otto_Fritsch-Denkmaeler_Deutscher_Renaissance-1891-Nuernberg-Pellerhaus_zu_Nuernberg_Aegidienplatz_1605_Facade.jpg/255px-Karl_Emil_Otto_Fritsch-Denkmaeler_Deutscher_Renaissance-1891-Nuernberg-Pellerhaus_zu_Nuernberg_Aegidienplatz_1605_Facade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Karl_Emil_Otto_Fritsch-Denkmaeler_Deutscher_Renaissance-1891-Nuernberg-Pellerhaus_zu_Nuernberg_Aegidienplatz_1605_Facade.jpg/340px-Karl_Emil_Otto_Fritsch-Denkmaeler_Deutscher_Renaissance-1891-Nuernberg-Pellerhaus_zu_Nuernberg_Aegidienplatz_1605_Facade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3863" data-file-height="5500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Karl_Emil_Otto_Fritsch-Denkmaeler_Deutscher_Renaissance-1891-Nuernberg-Pellerhaus_zu_Nuernberg_Aegidienplatz_1605_Facade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pellerhaus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pellerhaus (page does not exist)">Pellerhaus</a> in Nuremberg was one of the most important buildings of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance</a> period from 1605 until the destruction of its façade in 1945.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi era">Nazi era</a> Nuremberg played a prominent role in the self-expression of the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialists" class="mw-redirect" title="National Socialists">National Socialists</a> as the permanent seat of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gunzenhausen" title="Gunzenhausen">Gunzenhausen</a> made its mark as one of the first towns in the Reich itself to exercise discrimination against the Jewish population. The first Hitler Monument in the German Empire was established there in April 1933. On 25&#160;March 1934 the first <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">pogrom</a> in Bavaria took place in Gunzenhausen. The attack brought the town negative press coverage worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-N.C3.BCrnberger_Nachrichten_0309_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-N.C3.BCrnberger_Nachrichten_0309-107">[106]</a></sup> On 15&#160;September, a <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_(Nazi_Germany)" title="Reichstag (Nazi Germany)">Reichstag</a> was specially convened in Nuremberg for the purpose of passing the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>, under which the <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitic</a> ideology of the Nazis became a legal basis for such actions.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Like all parts of the German Reich, Franconia was badly affected by <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> <a href="/wiki/Airstrike" title="Airstrike">air raids</a>. Nuremberg, as a major industrial centre and transportation hub, was hit particularly hard. Between 1940 and 1945 the city was the target of dozens of air raids. Many other places were also affected by air raids. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Air_raid_on_Heilbronn" class="mw-redirect" title="Air raid on Heilbronn">air raid on 4 December 1944</a> on Heilbronn<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_W%C3%BCrzburg_on_16_March_1945" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombing of Würzburg on 16 March 1945">bombing of Würzburg on 16&#160;March 1945</a>, in which both old towns were almost completely destroyed, was a disaster for both cities. By contrast, the old town of Bamberg was almost completely spared.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> In order to protect <a href="/wiki/Cultural_artefact" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural artefact">cultural artefacts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Historischer_Kunstbunker" title="Historischer Kunstbunker">historic art bunker</a> was built below Nuremberg Castle.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> In the closing stages of the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, at the end of March and April 1945, Franconian towns and cities were captured by formations of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">US Army</a> who advanced from the west after the failure of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bulge" title="Battle of the Bulge">Battle of the Bulge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Nordwind" title="Operation Nordwind">Operation Nordwind</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nuremberg_(1945)" title="Battle of Nuremberg (1945)">Battle of Nuremberg</a> lasted five days and resulted in at least 901 deaths. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Crailsheim&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Battle of Crailsheim (page does not exist)">Battle of Crailsheim</a> lasted 16&#160;days, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_W%C3%BCrzburg_(1945)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Battle of Würzburg (1945) (page does not exist)">Battle of Würzburg</a> seven and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Merkendorf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Battle of Merkendorf (page does not exist)">Battle of Merkendorf</a> three&#160;days.</p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Unconditional_surrender_of_the_Wehrmacht" class="mw-redirect" title="Unconditional surrender of the Wehrmacht">unconditional surrender</a> on 8&#160;May 1945, Bavarian Franconia became part of the <a href="/wiki/American_zone_of_occupation" class="mw-redirect" title="American zone of occupation">American zone of occupation</a>; whilst South Thuringia, with the exception of smaller enclaves like <a href="/wiki/Ostheim" title="Ostheim">Ostheim</a>, became part of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet zone">Soviet zone</a> and the Franconian parts of today's Baden-Württemberg also went to the American zone<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> The most important part of the Allied prosecution programme against leaders of the Nazi regime were the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Trials" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg Trials">Nuremberg Trials</a> against leaders of the German Empire during the Nazi era, held from 20 November 1945 to 14 April 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> The Nuremberg Trials are considered a breakthrough for the principle that, for a core set of crimes, there is no <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_immunity" title="Diplomatic immunity">immunity</a> from prosecution. For the first time the representatives of a <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign</a> state were held accountable for their actions. In autumn 1946, the Free State of Bavaria was reconstituted with the enactment of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bavaria" title="Constitution of Bavaria">Bavarian Constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state of <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg-Baden" title="Württemberg-Baden">Württemberg-Baden</a> was founded on 19&#160;September 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> On 25&#160;April 1952 this state merged with <a href="/wiki/Baden_(South_Baden)" class="mw-redirect" title="Baden (South Baden)">Baden</a> and <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg-Hohenzollern" title="Württemberg-Hohenzollern">Württemberg-Hohenzollern</a> (both from the former <a href="/wiki/French_occupation_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="French occupation zone">French occupation zone</a>) to create the present state of Baden-Württemberg.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> On 1&#160;December 1945 the state of Hesse was founded. Beginning in 1945, <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_(1944%E2%80%9350)" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans (1944–50)">refugees and displaced persons from Eastern Europe</a> were settled particularly in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> After 1945, Bavaria and Baden-Württemberg managed the transition from economies that were predominantly <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> to become leading industrial states in the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Wirtschaftswunder" title="Wirtschaftswunder">Wirtschaftswunder</a></i>. In Lower and Upper Franconia, there was still the problem, however, of the zone along the <a href="/wiki/Inner_German_Border" class="mw-redirect" title="Inner German Border">Inner German Border</a> which was a long way from the markets for its agricultural produce, and was affected by migration and relatively high unemployment,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> which is why these areas received special support from federal and state governments.</p>
<p>By contrast, the state of Thuringia was restored by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Military_Administration_in_Germany" title="Soviet Military Administration in Germany">Soviets</a> in 1945. On 7&#160;October 1949 the <a href="/wiki/German_Democratic_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="German Democratic Republic">German Democratic Republic</a>, commonly known as <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>, was founded. In 1952 in the course of the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_East_Germany" title="Administrative divisions of East Germany">1952 administrative reform in East Germany</a>,the state of Thuringia was relieved of its function<sup id="cite_ref-Thuringia_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thuringia-119">[118]</a></sup> The Soviet <a href="/w/index.php?title=Occupying_forces&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Occupying forces (page does not exist)">occupying forces</a> exacted a high level of reparations (especially the <a href="/wiki/Allied_plans_for_German_industry_after_World_War_II" title="Allied plans for German industry after World War II">dismantling</a> of industrial facilities) which made the initial economic conditions in East Germany very difficult.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> Along with the failed economic policies of the GDR, this led to a general frustration that fuelled the <a href="/wiki/Uprising_of_17_June" class="mw-redirect" title="Uprising of 17 June">uprising of 17 June</a>. There were protests in the Franconian territories too, for example in Schmalkalden.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> The village of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6dlareuth" title="Mödlareuth">Mödlareuth</a> became famous because, for 41&#160;years, it was divided by the <a href="/wiki/Inner_German_Border" class="mw-redirect" title="Inner German Border">Inner German Border</a> and was nicknamed 'Little Berlin. After <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Wende" title="Die Wende">Die Wende</a></i>, the fall of the Berlin Wall on 9 November 1989 and <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunification</a> on 3&#160;October 1990, made possible mainly by mass demonstrations in East Germany and local exodus of East Germans, the state of Thuringia was reformed with effect from 14 October 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-Thuringia_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thuringia-119">[118]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zusammensetzung_des_Landkreises_Ansbach.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Zusammensetzung_des_Landkreises_Ansbach.png/220px-Zusammensetzung_des_Landkreises_Ansbach.png" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Zusammensetzung_des_Landkreises_Ansbach.png/330px-Zusammensetzung_des_Landkreises_Ansbach.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Zusammensetzung_des_Landkreises_Ansbach.png/440px-Zusammensetzung_des_Landkreises_Ansbach.png 2x" data-file-width="1027" data-file-height="957" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zusammensetzung_des_Landkreises_Ansbach.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The administrative reform in Bavaria in the Franconian county of <a href="/wiki/Landkreis_Ansbach" class="mw-redirect" title="Landkreis Ansbach">Ansbach</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the years from 1971 to 1980 an administrative reform was carried out in Bavaria with the aim of creating more efficient municipalities (<i><a href="/wiki/Gemeinde_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gemeinde (Germany)">Gemeinden</a></i>) and counties (<i><a href="/wiki/Landkreis" class="mw-redirect" title="Landkreis">Landkreise</a></i>). Against sometimes great protests by the population the number of municipalities was reduced by a third and the number of counties by about a half. Among the changes was the transfer of the Middle Franconian county of <a href="/wiki/Landkreis_Eichst%C3%A4tt" class="mw-redirect" title="Landkreis Eichstätt">Eichstätt</a> to <a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">Upper Bavaria</a>. On 18 May 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Landtag" class="mw-redirect" title="Bavarian Landtag">Bavarian Landtag</a> approved the introduction of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Franconia Day (page does not exist)">Franconia Day</a> (<i>Tag der Franken</i>) in the Franconian territories of the free state.<sup id="cite_ref-einf.C3.BChrungtagderfranken_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-einf.C3.BChrungtagderfranken-122">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since <i>Die Wende</i>, new markets have opened up for the Franconian region of Bavaria in the new (formerly East German) federal states and the Czech Republic, enabling the economy to recover.<sup id="cite_ref-grenzland_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grenzland-123">[122]</a></sup> Today, Franconia is in the centre of the EU (at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Oberwestern&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oberwestern (page does not exist)">Oberwestern</a> near <a href="/wiki/Westerngrund" title="Westerngrund">Westerngrund</a>; <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Franconia&amp;params=50.117286_N_9.247768_E_type:landmark_text:location_region:DE-BY_name:">geographical centre of the EU <span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">50°07′02″N</span> <span class="longitude">9°14′52″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">50.117286°N 9.247768°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">50.117286; 9.247768</span></span></span></a></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_Franconia">Contemporary Franconia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Contemporary Franconia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>While <a href="/wiki/Old_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Bavaria">Old Bavaria</a> is overwhelmingly <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, Franconia is a mixed area. Lower Franconia and the western half of Upper Franconia (<a href="/wiki/Bamberg" title="Bamberg">Bamberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lichtenfels,_Bavaria" title="Lichtenfels, Bavaria">Lichtenfels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kronach" title="Kronach">Kronach</a>) is predominantly Catholic, while most of Middle and the eastern half of Upper Franconia (<a href="/wiki/Bayreuth" title="Bayreuth">Bayreuth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hof,_Bavaria" title="Hof, Bavaria">Hof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kulmbach" title="Kulmbach">Kulmbach</a>) are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> (<a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">Evangelical Church in Germany</a>). The city of <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrth" title="Fürth">Fürth</a> in Middle Franconia historically (before the Nazi era) had a large <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> population; <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kissinger" title="Henry Kissinger">Henry Kissinger</a> was born there.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A large part of the population of Franconia, which has a population of five million,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> consider themselves Franconians (<i>Franken</i>, in German homonymous with the name of the historical <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>), a sub-ethnic group of the <a href="/wiki/German_people" class="mw-redirect" title="German people">German people</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Alemanni" title="Alemanni">Alemanni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swabians" title="Swabians">Swabians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavarians" title="Bavarians">Bavarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thuringians" class="mw-redirect" title="Thuringians">Thuringians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>. Such an ethnic identity is generally not shared by other parts of the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_languages" title="Franconian languages">Franconian-speaking</a> area (members of which may identify as Rhine Franconians (<i>Rheinfranken</i>) or Moselle Franconians (<i>Moselfranken</i>).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Free_State_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Free State of Bavaria">Free State of Bavaria</a> counts Franconians as one of the "four tribes of Bavaria" (<i>vier Stämme Bayerns</i>), alongside Bavarians, Swabians and <a href="/wiki/Sudeten_Germans" title="Sudeten Germans">Sudeten Germans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Towns_and_cities">Towns and cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Towns and cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the exception of <a href="/wiki/Heilbronn" title="Heilbronn">Heilbronn</a>, all cities in Franconia and all towns with a population of over 50,000 are within the Free State of Bavaria. The five cities of Franconia are <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrth" title="Fürth">Fürth</a>, Heilbronn and <a href="/wiki/Erlangen" title="Erlangen">Erlangen</a>. In Middle Franconia, in the metropolitan region of Nuremberg there is a densely populated urban area consisting of Nuremberg, Fürth, Erlangen and <a href="/wiki/Schwabach" title="Schwabach">Schwabach</a>. Nuremberg is the fourteenth largest city in Germany and the second largest in Bavaria.</p>
<p>The largest settlements in Baden-Württemberg's Franconian region are Heilbronn (pop: 117,531), <a href="/wiki/Schw%C3%A4bisch_Hall" title="Schwäbisch Hall">Schwäbisch Hall</a> (37,096) and <a href="/wiki/Crailsheim" title="Crailsheim">Crailsheim</a> (32,417).<sup id="cite_ref-bw-einwohner_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-einwohner-127">[126]</a></sup> The largest places in the Thuringian part are <a href="/wiki/Suhl" title="Suhl">Suhl</a> (35,665), <a href="/wiki/Sonneberg" title="Sonneberg">Sonneberg</a> (23,796) and <a href="/wiki/Meiningen" title="Meiningen">Meiningen</a> (20,966).<sup id="cite_ref-th.C3.BC-einw_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-th.C3.BC-einw-128">[127]</a></sup> The largest place in the Hessian part of Franconia is <a href="/wiki/Gersfeld_(Rh%C3%B6n)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gersfeld (Rhön)">Gersfeld</a> with just 5,512&#160;inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> The largest cities within Bavaria are Nuremberg (495,121), Würzburg (124,577), Fürth (118,358) and Erlangen (105,412).<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> Franconia, with its numerous towns, was separate and not part of other territories such as the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">Duchy of Bavaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-st.C3.A4dte_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st.C3.A4dte-131">[130]</a></sup> In the late medieval period it was dominated by mainly smaller towns with a few hundred to a thousand inhabitants, whose size barely distinguished them from the villages. Many towns grew up along large rivers or were founded by the prince-bishops and nobility. Even the <a href="/wiki/Hohenstaufens" class="mw-redirect" title="Hohenstaufens">Hohenstaufens</a> operated in many towns, most of which later became <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Cities">Imperial Cities</a> with a strong orientation towards Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-st.C3.A4dte_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st.C3.A4dte-131">[130]</a></sup> The smallest town in Franconia is Thuringia's <a href="/wiki/Ummerstadt" title="Ummerstadt">Ummerstadt</a> with 487 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-th.C3.BC-einw_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-th.C3.BC-einw-128">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ostfraenkischer_Sprachraum.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Ostfraenkischer_Sprachraum.png/240px-Ostfraenkischer_Sprachraum.png" width="240" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Ostfraenkischer_Sprachraum.png/360px-Ostfraenkischer_Sprachraum.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Ostfraenkischer_Sprachraum.png/480px-Ostfraenkischer_Sprachraum.png 2x" data-file-width="1180" data-file-height="825" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ostfraenkischer_Sprachraum.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Distribution of the East Franconian dialects with transition zones</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>German is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> and also the <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i>. Numerous other languages are spoken that come from other language regions or the native countries of immigrants.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/East_Franconian_German" title="East Franconian German">East Franconian German</a>, the dialect spoken in Franconia, is very different from the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Bavarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Bavarian">Austro-Bavarian</a> dialect. Most Franconians do not call themselves Bavarians. Even though there is no Franconian state, red and white are regarded as the state colours (<i><a href="/wiki/Landesfarben" title="Landesfarben">Landesfarben</a></i>) of Franconia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Christianity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The proportion of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">Protestants</a> among the population of Franconia is roughly the same, but varies from region to region.<sup id="cite_ref-religion_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion-132">[131]</a></sup> Large areas of Middle and Upper Franconia are mainly Protestant.<sup id="cite_ref-religion_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion-132">[131]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Religious_denomination" title="Religious denomination">denominational</a> orientation today still reflects the territorial structure of Franconia at the time of the Franconian Circle. For example, regions, that used to be under the care of the bishoprics of Bamberg, Würzburg and Eichstätt, are mainly Catholic today. On the other hand, all former territories of the imperial cities and the margraviates of Ansbach and Bayreuth have remained mainly Lutheran. The region around the city of <a href="/wiki/Erlangen" title="Erlangen">Erlangen</a>, which belonged to the Margraviate of Bayreuth, was a refuge for the <a href="/wiki/Huguenot" class="mw-redirect" title="Huguenot">Huguenots</a> who fled there after the <a href="/wiki/St._Bartholomew%27s_Day_massacre" title="St. Bartholomew's Day massacre">St. Bartholomew's Day massacre</a> in France.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> Following the success of <a href="/wiki/The_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="The Reformation">the Reformation</a> in Nuremberg under <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Osiander" title="Andreas Osiander">Andreas Osiander</a>, it had been an exclusively Protestant imperial city and belonged to the Protestant league of imperial states, the <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Evangelicorum" title="Corpus Evangelicorum">Corpus Evangelicorum</a>, within the <i><a href="/wiki/Reichstag_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Reichstag (Holy Roman Empire)">Reichstag</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-lex_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lex-134">[133]</a></sup> Subsequent historical events such as the <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_(1944%E2%80%9350)" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans (1944–50)">stream of refugees</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> and the increasing mobility of the population have since blurred denominational geographical boundaries, however.</p>
<p>The influx of immigrants from Eastern Europe has also seen the establishment of an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a> community in Franconia. The Romanian Orthodox Metropolis of Germany, Central and Northern Europe has its headquarters in Nuremberg.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Judaism">Judaism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Judaism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi era">Nazi era</a> Franconia was as a region with significant Jewish communities, most of whom were <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-juden1_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-juden1-135">[134]</a></sup> The first Jewish communities appeared in Franconia in the 12th and 13th&#160;centuries and thus later than, for example, in <a href="/wiki/Regensburg" title="Regensburg">Regensburg</a>. In the Middle Ages, Franconia was a stronghold of <a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">Torah</a> studies. But Franconia also began to exclude the Jewish populations particularly early on. For example, there were two Jewish massacres - the <a href="/wiki/Rintfleisch_massacres" title="Rintfleisch massacres">Rintfleisch massacres</a> of 1298 and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Armleder_Uprising&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Armleder Uprising (page does not exist)">Armleder Uprising</a> of 1336-1338 - and in the 15th and 16th&#160;centuries many cities exiled their Jewish populations, which is why many Jews settled in rural communities. Franconia also rose to early prominence in the discrimination of Jews during the Nazi era.<sup id="cite_ref-juden2_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-juden2-136">[135]</a></sup> One of the first casualties of the organized Nazi persecution of Jews took place on 21&#160;March in <a href="/wiki/K%C3%BCnzelsau" title="Künzelsau">Künzelsau</a> and on 25/26&#160;March 1933 in <a href="/wiki/Creglingen" title="Creglingen">Creglingen</a>, where police and <a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">SA</a> troops under the leadership of <i><a href="/wiki/Standartenf%C3%BChrer" title="Standartenführer">Standartenführer</a></i> Fritz Klein so-called led a so-called "weapons search operations".<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> Whilst, in 1818, about 65&#160;per cent of Bavarian Jews lived in the Bavarian part of Franconia,<sup id="cite_ref-juden3_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-juden3-139">[138]</a></sup> today there are only Jewish communities in Bamberg, Bayreuth, Erlangen, Fürth, Hof, Nuremberg and Würzburg<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> and in Heilbronn in Baden-Württemberg.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Islam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Adherents of Islam continue to grow, especially in the larger cities, due to the influx of <i><a href="/wiki/Gastarbeiter" title="Gastarbeiter">gastarbeiters</a></i> and other <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrants</a> from Muslim countries. As a result, many 'backyard mosques' (<i>Hinterhofmoschees</i>) have sprung up, which are gradually being replaced by purpose-built <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Franconia has almost 300 small breweries.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> The northwestern parts, the areas around <a href="/wiki/River_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="River Main">river Main</a> called <a href="/wiki/Franconia_(wine_region)" title="Franconia (wine region)">Franconian wine region</a> also produce a lot of wine. <a href="/wiki/Franconian_cuisine" title="Franconian cuisine">Food typical for the region</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Bratwurst" title="Bratwurst">Bratwurst</a> (especially the famous small Nuremberger Bratwurst), <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%A4ufele" title="Schäufele"><i>Schäuferla</i></a> (stewed pork shoulder), <a href="/wiki/Sauerbraten" title="Sauerbraten">Sauerbraten</a>, dumplings, potato salad (typically made with <a href="/wiki/Broth" title="Broth">broth</a>), fried <a href="/wiki/Common_carp" title="Common carp">carp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obatzda" title="Obatzda">Grupfder</a> (seasoned cheese spread), <i>Presssack</i> (a type of <a href="/wiki/Head_cheese" title="Head cheese">Head cheese</a>: pressed or jellied pork trimmings, like tongue, cheeks, etc.). <a href="/wiki/Lebkuchen" title="Lebkuchen">Lebkuchen</a> are a traditional type of biscuit, and <a href="/wiki/Kniek%C3%BCchle" title="Knieküchle">Küchla</a> is a sort of sweet fried dough.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rothenburg_BW_4.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Rothenburg_BW_4.JPG/220px-Rothenburg_BW_4.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Rothenburg_BW_4.JPG/330px-Rothenburg_BW_4.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Rothenburg_BW_4.JPG/440px-Rothenburg_BW_4.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rothenburg_BW_4.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One of the best known tourist attractions in Franconia is the town of Rothenburg ob der Tauber</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlosslangenburgmsu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Schlosslangenburgmsu.jpg/220px-Schlosslangenburgmsu.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Schlosslangenburgmsu.jpg/330px-Schlosslangenburgmsu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Schlosslangenburgmsu.jpg/440px-Schlosslangenburgmsu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlosslangenburgmsu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/w/index.php?title=Schloss_Langenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Schloss Langenburg (page does not exist)">Schloss Langenburg</a> (Baden-Württemberg) lies on the <a href="/wiki/Castle_Road" title="Castle Road">Castle Road</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> industry stresses the romantic character of Franconia.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-franken-tourismus_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-franken-tourismus-143">[142]</a></sup> Arguments for this include the picturesque countryside and the many historic buildings that present the long history and culture of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-franken-tourismus_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-franken-tourismus-143">[142]</a></sup> In addition the relatively few industrial towns outside of the main industrial cities is underlined. <a href="/wiki/Franconian_wine" class="mw-redirect" title="Franconian wine">Franconian wine</a>, the rich tradition of beer brewing and local culinary specialities, such as <i>Lebküchnerei</i> or <a href="/wiki/Gingerbread" title="Gingerbread">gingerbread</a> baking, are also seen as a draw that is worth marketing,<sup id="cite_ref-franken-tourismus_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-franken-tourismus-143">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> and which make Franconia a popular tourist destination in Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Romantic_Road" title="Romantic Road">Romantic Road</a>, the best known German <a href="/wiki/Theme_route" class="mw-redirect" title="Theme route">theme route</a>, links several of the tourist high points in western Franconia.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Castle_Road" title="Castle Road">Castle Road</a> runs through the whole Franconian region with its numerous castles and other medieval structures.</p>
<p>The Franconian countryside is suitable for many sporting activities. For example, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconian_Way&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Franconian Way (page does not exist)">Franconian Way</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Way" title="Celtic Way">Celtic Way</a> and the hiking trail network of the <a href="/wiki/Altm%C3%BChl_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Altmühl Valley">Altmühl Valley</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central_Uplands" title="Central Uplands">Central Uplands</a> offer a lot of hiking options.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">Cycling</a> along the large rivers is very popular, for example along the <a href="/wiki/Main_Cycleway" title="Main Cycleway">Main Cycleway</a>, which was the first German long distance cycleway to be awarded five starts by the <a href="/wiki/Allgemeiner_Deutscher_Fahrrad-Club" title="Allgemeiner Deutscher Fahrrad-Club">Allgemeiner Deutscher Fahrrad-Club</a> (ADFC). The <a href="/wiki/Tauber_Valley_Cycleway" title="Tauber Valley Cycleway">Tauber Valley Cycleway</a>, a 101 kilometre-long <a href="/wiki/Cycle_trail" class="mw-redirect" title="Cycle trail">cycle trail</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tauber_Franconia" title="Tauber Franconia">Tauber Franconia</a>, was the second German long distance cycleway to receive five stars.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Franconia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-65">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">East Franconia should not be confused with the eastern division of the Frankish Empire, <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a>, which was also known as <i><span lang="la" xml:lang="la">Francia Orientalis</span></i> in Latin. This refers to the much larger area which later became the <a href="/wiki/German_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="German Kingdom">German Kingdom</a> and which the whole of the Duchy of Franconia was a part.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
</div>
